2:35:2482:0:14:72:303:700:12:Times:12:Times:Do Funds Make More When They Trade More?
2:36:2522:14:14:72:355:686:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:Lubos Pastor, Robert F. Stambaugh, and Lucian A. Taylor 
2:37:2577:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 20700
2:38:2605:14:14:72:249:658:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:November 2014, Revised April 2016
2:39:2638:14:28:72:179:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. G10,G20,J24
2:40:2657:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:41:2665:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:We model optimal fund turnover in the presence of time-varying profit opportunities. Our model 
2:42:2760:14:14:72:543:574:12:Times:12:Times:predicts a  positive  relation  between  an  active  fund’s  turnover  and  its  subsequent  benchmark-
2:43:2862:14:14:71:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:adjusted  return. We  find  such  a  relation  for  equity  mutual  funds.  This  time-series  relation 
2:44:2965:14:14:71:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:between  turnover  and  performance is  stronger  than  the  cross-sectional  relation,  as  the  model 
2:45:3068:14:14:72:542:532:12:Times:12:Times:predicts.  Also  as  predicted,  the  turnover-performance relation  is  stronger  for  funds  trading  less-
2:46:3176:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:liquid  stocks,  such  as  small-cap  funds.  Turnover  has  a  common component  that  is  positively 
2:47:3278:14:14:71:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:correlated  with  proxies  for  stock  mispricing,  consistent  with  funds  exploiting time-varying 
2:48:3378:14:28:71:424:490:12:Times:12:Times:opportunities. Turnover’s common component helps predict fund returns.
2:49:3448:28:14:72:135:462:12:Times:12:Times:Lubos Pastor
2:50:3460:14:14:72:179:448:12:Times:12:Times:University of Chicago
2:51:3481:14:14:72:196:434:12:Times:12:Times:Booth School of Business
2:52:3505:14:14:72:206:420:12:Times:12:Times:5807 South Woodlawn Ave
2:53:3528:14:14:72:165:406:12:Times:12:Times:Chicago, IL  60637
2:54:3546:14:14:72:124:392:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:55:3554:14:28:72:226:378:12:Times:12:Times:lubos.pastor@chicagobooth.edu
2:56:3583:28:14:72:174:350:12:Times:12:Times:Robert F. Stambaugh
2:57:3602:14:14:72:170:336:12:Times:12:Times:Finance Department
2:58:3620:14:14:72:172:322:12:Times:12:Times:The Wharton School

2:68:3841:14:14:306:395:392:12:Times:12:Times:3620 Locust Walk
2:69:3857:14:14:306:448:378:12:Times:12:Times:Philadelphia, PA 19104-6367

3:71:3907:0:41:72:209:723:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:1.  Introduction
3:72:3923:41:18:72:540:682:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Mutual funds invest trillions of dollars on behalf of retail investors. The lion’s share of this
3:73:4019:18:18:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:money is actively managed, despite the growing popularity of passive investing.1Whether
3:74:4106:18:17:72:540:646:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:skill guides the trades of actively managed funds has long been an important question, given
3:75:4198:17:18:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:active funds’ higher fees and trading costs. We take a fresh look at skill by analyzing time
3:76:4290:18:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:variation in active funds’ trading activity. We explore a simple idea: A fund trades more
3:77:4379:18:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when it perceives greater profit opportunities. If the fund has the ability to identify and
3:78:4470:18:29:72:526:575:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:exploit those opportunities, then it should earn greater profit after trading more heavily.
3:79:4561:29:18:89:540:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We formalize this idea by developing a model of fund trading in the presence of time-
3:80:4646:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:varying profit opportunities. Each period, funds identify opportunities to establish positions
3:81:4740:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that yield profits in the subsequent period, net of trading costs. A fund’s optimal amount
3:82:4830:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of turnover maximizes its expected net profit, conditional on equilibrium prices.  Profit
3:83:4919:18:18:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:opportunities vary over time, jointly determining turnover and performance. A fund trades
3:84:5008:18:18:72:540:456:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more in periods when it has more profit opportunities. Our model’s key implication is a
3:85:5095:18:28:72:516:438:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:positive time-series relation between optimally chosen turnover and subsequent return.
3:86:5181:28:18:89:540:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Consistent with the model, we find that a fund’s turnover positively predicts the fund’s
3:87:5269:18:18:72:540:392:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:subsequent benchmark-adjusted return. This new evidence of skill comes from our sample
3:88:5355:18:18:72:540:374:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of 3,126 active U.S. equity mutual funds from 1979 through 2011. The result is significant
3:89:5445:18:18:72:540:356:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not only statistically but also economically: a one-standard-deviation increase in turnover is
3:90:5539:18:18:72:540:338:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:associated with a 0.65% per year increase in performance for the typical fund. Funds seem
3:91:5628:18:29:72:276:320:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to know when it’s a good time to trade.
3:92:5667:29:18:89:539:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We focus on the time-series relation between turnover and performance for a given fund.
3:93:5754:18:18:72:540:273:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In contrast, prior studies ask whether there is a turnover-performance relation across funds.
3:94:5847:18:18:72:540:255:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The evidence on this cross-sectional relation is mixed. For example, Elton, Gruber, Das, and
3:95:5939:18:17:72:540:237:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Hlavka (1993) and Carhart (1997) find a negative relation, Wermers (2000), Kacperczyk,
3:96:6025:17:18:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Sialm, and Zheng (2005), and Edelen, Evans, and Kadlec (2007) find no significant relation,
3:97:6116:18:18:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Dahlquist, Engstr ̈om and S ̈oderlind (2000) and Chen, Jagadeesh and Wermers (2001)
3:98:6203:18:18:72:540:184:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:find a positive relation.  In accord with this mixed message, our sample delivers a weak
3:99:6291:18:29:72:391:166:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:positive cross-sectional relation, marginally significant at best.
3:100:6357:29:18:89:540:137:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Consistent with the empirical results, our model predicts that the time-series relation
3:101:6444:18:18:72:540:119:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between turnover and performance should be stronger than the cross-sectional relation. The
3:102:6534:18:15:85:540:101:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:1As of 2013, mutual funds worldwide have about $30 trillion of assets under management, half of which
3:103:6635:15:12:72:540:86:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:is managed by U.S. funds. About 52% of U.S. mutual fund assets are held in equity funds, and 81.6% of the
3:104:6740:12:0:72:467:74:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:equity funds’ total net assets are managed actively (Investment Company Institute, 2014).
4:105:6830:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:reason is that a given trade’s cost reduces current return, whereas its profit increases future
4:106:6925:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:return. Trading costs therefore do not dampen the time-series turnover-performance relation
4:107:7016:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as much as they dampen the cross-sectional relation, where the timing of profit and trading
4:108:7107:18:29:72:160:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cost is irrelevant.
4:109:7126:29:18:89:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our model also predicts that funds trading less-liquid stocks should have a stronger time-
4:110:7216:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:series relation between turnover and performance. The turnover of such funds optimally
4:111:7302:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:responds less to profit opportunities, so a given change in turnover implies a greater change
4:112:7395:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in profit opportunities. Consistent with this prediction, we find that funds holding stocks
4:113:7486:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of small companies, or small-cap funds, have a significantly stronger turnover-performance
4:114:7576:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relation than do large-cap funds. Similarly, we find a stronger relation for small funds than
4:115:7669:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:large funds, consistent with the ability of smaller funds to trade less-liquid stocks, given that
4:116:7766:18:29:72:308:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:smaller funds trade in smaller dollar amounts.
4:117:7812:29:18:89:540:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We find a stronger turnover-performance relation as well for funds charging higher fees.
4:118:7900:18:18:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This result has a skill-based interpretation, under the plausible assumption that funds with
4:119:7992:18:18:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:greater skill charge higher fees. If a less-skilled fund trades on profit opportunities that are
4:120:8088:18:18:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not really there, then some of the fund’s turnover is unrelated to expected future return.
4:121:8178:18:28:72:459:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The turnover-performance relation is therefore weaker for less-skilled funds.
4:122:8255:28:18:89:540:386:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We find strong evidence of commonality in fund turnover.  Turnover’s common com-
4:123:8335:18:18:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ponent appears to be related to mispricing in the stock market. Average turnover across
4:124:8422:18:18:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds—essentially the first principal component of turnover—is significantly related to three
4:125:8515:18:18:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:proxies for potential mispricing: investor sentiment, cross-sectional dispersion in individual
4:126:8609:18:18:72:540:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stock returns, and aggregate stock market liquidity. Funds trade more when sentiment or
4:127:8696:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:dispersion is high or liquidity is low, suggesting that stocks are more mispriced when funds
4:128:8788:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:collectively perceive greater profit opportunities. We also find that commonality in turnover
4:129:8881:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is especially high among funds sharing similar characteristics, suggesting more comovement
4:130:8971:18:29:72:293:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in profit opportunities across similar funds.
4:131:9016:29:17:89:539:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Average turnover positively predicts a fund’s future return, even when we control for the
4:132:9105:17:18:72:540:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s own turnover. This predictive relation is significant: a one-standard-deviation increase
4:133:9200:18:18:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in average turnover is associated with a 0.71% per year increase in fund performance. The
4:134:9289:18:29:72:514:160:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relation is even stronger when average turnover is computed only across similar funds.
4:135:9375:29:18:89:539:131:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The predictive ability of average turnover is consistent with the presence of error in our
4:136:9465:18:18:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:empirical measure of an individual fund’s turnover. This measure aims to exclude trades aris-
4:137:9558:18:18:72:540:95:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ing from a fund’s inflows and outflows, thereby reflecting only trades arising from the fund’s
4:138:9652:18:0:72:540:77:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:decisions to replace some stocks with others, but this objective can be accomplished only
5:139:9742:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:imperfectly. The common component of individual fund turnover—average turnover—helps
5:140:9826:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:capture a fund’s true turnover and thus helps to predict the fund’s performance. Measure-
5:141:9915:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ment error can also explain our finding that a fund’s performance is predicted even more
5:142:10003:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:strongly by the average turnover of similar funds. Since commonality in turnover is greater
5:143:10094:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:among similar funds, average turnover of similar funds is particularly useful in capturing a
5:144:10186:18:28:72:372:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s true turnover in the presence of measurement error.
5:145:10244:28:18:89:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Average turnover should also predict returns if funds trade suboptimally in that only a
5:146:10331:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:portion of their trading exploits true profit opportunities. If those opportunities are cor-
5:147:10423:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:related across funds while funds’ trading mistakes are not, then higher average turnover
5:148:10511:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:indicates greater profit opportunities in general. Any opportunity identified by a given fund
5:149:10604:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is likely to be more profitable if there is generally more mispricing at that time, as indicated
5:150:10700:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by other funds’ heavy trading. Suboptimal trading can also explain the superior predictive
5:151:10790:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:power of similar funds’ average turnover, as that turnover reflects especially relevant profit
5:152:10884:18:29:72:305:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:opportunities—those shared by similar funds.
5:153:10928:29:18:89:539:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The literature investigating the skill of active mutual funds is extensive. Average past
5:154:11016:18:18:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance delivers a seemingly negative verdict, since many studies show that active funds
5:155:11108:18:18:72:540:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:have underperformed passive benchmarks, net of fees.2Yet active funds can have skill.
5:156:11193:18:18:72:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Skilled funds might charge higher fees, and some funds might be more skilled than others.
5:157:11282:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Moreover, with fund-level or industry-level decreasing returns to scale, skill does not equate
5:158:11376:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to average performance, either gross or net of fees.3Our finding of a significant positive
5:159:11466:17:29:72:516:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time-series relation between turnover and performance provides novel evidence of skill.
5:160:11553:29:18:89:540:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:While we find that funds perform better after increasing their trading activity, others
5:161:11640:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:have related fund activity to performance in different ways. Kacperczyk, Sialm, and Zheng
5:162:11729:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(2005) find that funds that are more active in the sense of having more concentrated port-
5:163:11819:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:folios perform better. Kacperczyk, Sialm, and Zheng (2008) find that a fund’s actions be-
5:164:11908:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tween portfolio disclosure dates, as summarized by the “return gap,” positively predict fund
5:165:12000:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance. Cremers and Petajisto (2009) find that funds that deviate more from their
5:166:12086:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:benchmarks, as measured by “active share,” perform better. Cremers, Ferreira, Matos, and
5:167:12174:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Starks (2016) find similar results. In the same spirit, Amihud and Goyenko (2013) find bet-
5:168:12265:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ter performance among funds having lower R-squareds from benchmark regressions. These
5:169:12350:18:17:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:studies are similar to ours in that they also find that more active funds perform better, but
5:170:12443:17:18:72:540:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:there are two important differences. First, all of these studies measure fund activity in ways
5:171:12537:18:16:85:540:117:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:2See, for example, Jensen (1968), Elton, Gruber, Das, and Hlavka (1993), Malkiel (1995), Gruber (1996),
5:172:12640:16:8:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:Carhart (1997), Wermers (2000), P ́astor and Stambaugh (2002), and Fama and French (2010), among others.
5:173:12744:8:16:85:540:93:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:3See Berk and Green (2004), P ́astor and Stambaugh (2012), Stambaugh (2014), Berk and van Binsbergen
5:174:12844:16:0:72:296:77:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:(2015), and P ́astor, Stambaugh, and Taylor (2015).
6:175:12896:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:different from ours. Second, all of them identify cross-sectional relations between activity
6:176:12988:18:29:72:385:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and performance, whereas we establish a time-series relation.
6:177:13049:29:18:89:540:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Given this time-series perspective, our study is also related to the literature on time
6:178:13136:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:variation in mutual fund performance. Some authors, inspired by Ferson and Schadt (1996),
6:179:13225:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model performance as a linear function of conditioning variables (e.g., Avramov and Wer-
6:180:13313:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mers, 2006). Others relate fund performance to the business cycle (e.g., Moskowitz, 2000,
6:181:13402:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Glode, 2011, Kosowski, 2011, and Kacperczyk, van Nieuwerburgh, and Veldkamp, 2016),
6:182:13485:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to aggregate market returns (Glode, Hollifield, Kacperczyk, and Kogan, 2012), and to time
6:183:13574:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:variation in fund risk (e.g., Brown, Harlow, and Starks, 1996, and Huang, Sialm, and Zhang,
6:184:13665:18:29:72:435:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:2011). None of these studies relate fund performance to fund turnover.
6:185:13735:29:18:89:539:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:While we analyze funds’ ability to time their turnover, others have investigated the
6:186:13819:18:18:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:value of active fund management by examining different fund actions.  Chen, Jegadeesh,
6:187:13905:18:18:72:540:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Wermers (2000) find that stocks recently bought by funds in aggregate outperform
6:188:13989:18:18:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stocks recently sold, suggesting that funds have stock-picking skill. Baker et al. (2010) find
6:189:14083:18:18:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that much of this outperformance takes place around corporate earnings announcements,
6:190:14168:18:18:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:indicating one likely source of the funds’ skill. Cohen, Coval, and P ́astor (2005) find that
6:191:14261:18:18:72:540:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds whose portfolio decisions are similar to those of other funds with strong track records
6:192:14354:18:18:72:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:perform better. Alexander, Cici, and Gibson (2007) show that funds’ valuation-motivated
6:193:14441:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:buys (i.e., large stock buys concurrent with heavy fund outflows) outperform benchmarks
6:194:14528:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereas liquidity-motivated buys do not. Cohen, Frazzini, and Malloy (2008) find that fund
6:195:14618:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:managers perform better when they trade shares of firms they are connected to through
6:196:14703:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:their educational networks. Like us, all of these studies report that active management adds
6:197:14795:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:value, but they examine different dimensions of fund skill. Our finding that funds are able
6:198:14886:18:29:72:429:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to successfully time their trading activity seems new in the literature.
6:199:14958:29:18:89:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Lastly, our analysis of the common variation in fund turnover is related to the literature
6:200:15048:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on correlated trading behavior of mutual funds, or “herding.” Early studies include Nofsinger
6:201:15141:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Sias (1999) and Wermers (1999). More recently, Koch, Ruenzi, and Starks (2016) and
6:202:15227:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Karolyi, Lee, and van Dijk (2012) argue that such correlated trading gives rise to common-
6:203:15317:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ality in liquidity among stocks. Commonality in individual stock turnover is analyzed by Lo
6:204:15408:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Wang (2000), Cremers and Mei (2007), and others. None of these studies examine fund
6:205:15495:18:28:72:461:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover. Our analysis of the common component of fund turnover is novel.
6:206:15568:28:18:89:540:124:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The rest of the paper is organized as follows. Section 2 presents our model, which implies
6:207:15658:18:18:72:540:106:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a positive relation between a fund’s turnover and subsequent return.  Section 3 reports
6:208:15745:18:0:72:540:88:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:strong evidence of such a relation in our mutual fund sample and, in the context of our
7:209:15833:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model, contrasts the time-series relation with the weaker cross-sectional relation. Section
7:210:15924:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:4 explores differences in the strength of the time-series relation across categories of funds
7:211:16017:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:differentiated by size, fees, and investment styles. Section 5 analyzes the common component
7:212:16109:18:43:72:479:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of fund turnover and its predictive power for fund returns. Section 6 concludes.
7:213:16189:43:40:72:486:626:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:2.  Model of the Turnover-Performance Relation
7:214:16235:40:18:72:540:586:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In this section we present a simple model of optimal fund turnover in the presence of
7:215:16320:18:18:72:540:568:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time-varying profit opportunities. A manager trades more when he identifies more alpha-
7:216:16407:18:18:72:540:550:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:producing opportunities, so a skilled manager should perform better after he trades more.
7:217:16496:18:18:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The model implies a positive turnover-performance relation: a time-series regression in which
7:218:16589:18:44:72:432:514:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a fund’s turnover is positively related to the fund’s subsequent return.
7:219:16661:44:37:72:389:470:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.1  Profit Opportunities and Trading Costs
7:220:16704:37:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Active mutual funds pursue alpha—profit in excess of their benchmarks. A fund perceives
7:221:16791:18:18:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:opportunities for producing alpha and trades to exploit them. LetXtdenote a given level
7:222:16878:18:18:72:540:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of turnover that the fund can choose in periodt. LetP(Xt) denote the resulting expected
7:223:16965:18:18:72:539:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:benchmark-adjusted profit (alpha) in periodt+ 1, before fees and trading costs, if the fund
7:224:17056:18:17:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:makes optimal buy-sell decisions conditional on its turnover beingXt. The profit represented
7:225:17148:17:18:72:539:344:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:byP(Xt) reflects the fund’s ability to exploit opportunities in periodtfor which the payoff
7:226:17239:18:18:72:539:326:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:occurs in periodt+ 1. A prime example is a purchase of underpriced securities in periodt
7:227:17327:18:29:72:376:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:followed by the correction of the mispricing in periodt+ 1.
7:228:17386:29:18:89:540:279:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:If the fund wishes to maintain a well diversified portfolio of stocks, the fund is likely to
7:229:17478:18:18:72:540:261:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:replace more of its stocks whenXtis high than whenXtis low. As the fund moves further
7:230:17563:18:18:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:down its list of potential stocks to buy, the alphas on the additional stocks are likely to be
7:231:17657:18:18:72:540:225:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lower than those on stocks higher up the fund’s list. As a result,P(Xt) is likely to be concave
7:232:17752:18:23:72:331:207:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inXt. We represent this concave profit function as
7:233:17802:23:24:262:540:184:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:P(Xt) =πtX1−θt,(1)
7:234:17820:24:17:72:540:160:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where 0< θ <1. Variation over time in the fund’s profit opportunities is summarized by
7:235:17906:17:29:72:503:143:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the parameterπt. The higher isπt, the more profitable are the fund’s opportunities.
7:236:17989:29:18:89:539:114:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:LetC(Xt) denote the trading cost in periodtincurred by the fund as a result of turning
7:237:18075:18:24:72:406:96:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:overXtin that period. We represent the trading cost function as
7:238:18138:24:0:264:540:72:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:C(Xt) =cX1+γt,(2)
8:239:18156:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereγ≥0. We allow this function to be convex because it is generally accepted that the
8:240:18243:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cost of trading a given stock is convex in the amount of that stock traded (e.g., Kyle and
8:241:18333:18:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Obizhaeva (2013)). To the extent that a higher value ofXtcorresponds to the fund trading
8:242:18421:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more of any given stock, we would expect some convexity inC(Xt). On the other hand, if a
8:243:18509:18:18:72:539:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher value ofXtcorresponds to the fund mainly replacing a greater number of its stocks,
8:244:18598:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as opposed to trading a greater amount of any given stock, thenC(Xt) should be close to
8:245:18685:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:linear. That is,γshould be close to zero. As we explain below, a near-zero value ofγis
8:246:18771:18:45:72:465:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:consistent with our empirical evidence on the turnover-performance relation.
8:247:18847:45:36:72:236:552:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.2  Optimal Turnover
8:248:18868:36:18:72:539:516:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The fund’s chosen level of turnover maximizes expected next-period profit net of the current
8:249:18960:18:18:72:540:498:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:trading cost incurred to produce that profit. We assume that the fund maximizes this after-
8:250:19051:18:18:72:540:480:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cost profit before subtracting fees charged to investors.4Recall thatP(Xt) in equation (1)
8:251:19141:18:29:72:501:462:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is profit before both fees and trading costs. The fund’s choice ofXttherefore solves
8:252:19225:29:7:244:266:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:max
8:253:19228:7:0:250:260:426:8:g_d0_f9:6:g_d0_f12:Xt
8:254:19230:0:29:270:540:433:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f4:{P(Xt)−C(Xt)}.(3)
8:255:19247:29:28:72:517:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This objective function is concave and hump-shaped inXt. The first-order condition is
8:256:19332:28:29:222:540:376:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:πt(1−θ)X−θt−c(1 +γ)Xγt= 0,(4)
8:257:19361:29:36:72:291:347:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from which the optimal level of turnover is
8:258:19404:36:0:247:275:311:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:X∗t=
8:259:19408:0:10:278:284:329:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:[
8:260:19409:10:16:286:331:319:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:πt(1−θ)
8:261:19416:16:0:288:329:303:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:c(1 +γ)
8:262:19423:0:18:332:353:329:10:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f12:]1θ+γ
8:263:19428:18:33:360:540:311:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:.(5)
8:264:19432:33:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We see that the fund trades more when its profit opportunities are better (i.e., whenπtis
8:265:19521:18:28:72:502:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher). Also, higher trading costs (c) imply less trading. Both results are intuitive.
8:266:19608:28:18:89:540:232:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:When the fund decides how much to trade, it conditions on equilibrium prices. We do
8:267:19691:18:18:72:540:214:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not model the formation of equilibrium prices, which reflect the joint effects of all funds’
8:268:19783:18:18:72:540:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:trading. Instead, we rely on a simple point: Whatever the price formation process, if equi-
8:269:19874:18:18:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:librium prices do not offer the fund a higher net profit at the fund’s chosen level of turnover
8:270:19969:18:18:72:540:160:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than at any other level of turnover, then the fund is not optimizing. When specifying the
8:271:20058:18:18:72:540:142:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s optimization problem in equation (3), we assume there are many funds and that any
8:272:20146:18:18:72:540:124:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:individual fund takes equilibrium prices—and thus its own after-cost profit opportunities—
8:273:20236:18:18:72:539:106:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as given when deciding how much to trade. In other words,C(Xt) does not represent price
8:274:20323:18:16:85:540:88:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:4One justification for this assumption is that a higher profit before fees essentially provides the fund with
8:275:20432:16:0:72:515:72:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:a higher fee, if fund flows result in zero net alpha provided to investors, as in Berk and Green (2004).
9:276:20537:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:impact that affects the equilibrium prices on which the fund conditions.  Rather,C(Xt)
9:277:20623:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is best viewed as compensation to liquidity-providing intermediaries for taking short-lived
9:278:20714:18:45:72:532:687:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:positions to facilitate the ultimate market clearing between the fund and other investors.5
9:279:20805:45:37:72:332:642:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.3  Turnover-Performance Relation
9:280:20839:37:32:72:473:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To relate turnover to performance, we first solve equation (5)forπt, obtaining
9:281:20917:32:0:245:267:573:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:πt=
9:282:20920:0:16:272:314:581:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:c(1 +γ)
9:283:20927:16:0:275:311:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(1−θ)
9:284:20932:0:33:316:540:573:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(X∗t)θ+γ.(6)
9:285:20944:33:32:72:513:540:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Substituting forπtinto equation (1) whenXt=X∗tthen gives the time-series relation
9:286:21025:32:0:234:280:508:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:P(X∗t) =
9:287:21033:0:16:285:326:516:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:c(1 +γ)
9:288:21040:16:0:292:318:500:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:1−θ
9:289:21043:0:30:329:540:508:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(X∗t)1+γ.(7)
9:290:21055:30:18:72:540:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The profit and cost given by equations (1) and (2) can be viewed as being scaled by the
9:291:21142:18:18:72:540:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s assets, so that they represent contributions to the fund’s rate of return. With that
9:292:21233:18:18:72:540:442:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:normalization, the fund’s overall before-fee realized return in periodt+1,Rt+1, equalsP(X∗t)
9:293:21325:18:18:72:540:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:plus a mean-zero deviation minusC(X∗t+1), the trading costs associated with the optimal
9:294:21412:18:32:72:426:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover chosen in periodt+ 1. That is, using equations (2) and (7),
9:295:21480:32:0:188:223:374:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Rt+1=
9:296:21485:0:16:228:269:382:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:c(1 +γ)
9:297:21492:16:0:235:261:366:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:1−θ
9:298:21495:0:29:272:540:374:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(X∗t)1+γ−c(X∗t+1)1+γ+ηt+1,(8)
9:299:21524:29:18:72:540:345:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereηt+1is the mean-zero deviation of realized before-cost profit from its expectation. We
9:300:21615:18:18:72:540:327:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assume that profit opportunities vary over time in a manner that allows the conditional
9:301:21702:18:29:72:358:309:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mean of (X∗t+1)1+γgivenX∗tto be well approximated as
9:302:21754:29:29:198:540:280:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:E{(X∗t+1)1+γ|X∗t}=μ(1−ρ) +ρ(X∗t)1+γ,(9)

9:313:21973:29:18:72:540:171:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:As noted earlier,γis likely to be close to zero if higher turnover largely corresponds to
9:314:22062:18:18:72:540:153:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:replacing a greater number of stocks rather than buying more of a given set of stocks. We
9:315:22151:18:18:72:540:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:see from (10) that a near-zeroγdelivers a near-linear relation between turnover (X∗t) and
9:316:22240:18:16:85:540:117:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:5One might imagine funds trading with many intermediaries who access different sources of liquidity or
9:317:22342:16:11:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:act at slightly different times. A similar approach is taken by Stambaugh (2014) in a general equilibrium
9:318:22447:11:14:72:289:90:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:model of active management and price formation.
9:319:22494:14:0:85:381:76:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f15:6From (5), we see that a sufficient condition for this result is thatπ
9:320:22564:0:13:382:394:83:5:g_d0_f16:5:g_d0_f17:1+γγ+θ

10:322:22597:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:expected return. Our empirical analysis reveals no significant departure from linearity in
10:323:22687:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the turnover-performance relation, consistent with the assumption ofγ≈0.  Given this
10:324:22771:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assumption, from (9) we see thatμ= E(X∗t) andρis the autocorrelation ofX∗t.  With
10:325:22852:18:30:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:γ≈0, the turnover-performance relation in (10) is well represented by the linear regression
10:326:22943:30:30:245:540:639:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Rt+1=a+bX∗t+-t+1,(11)
10:327:22964:30:18:72:193:609:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where E(-t+1|X∗t) = 0 ,
10:328:22987:18:24:252:540:591:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:a=−c(1−ρ)E(X∗t),(12)
10:329:23007:24:18:72:91:567:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and

10:331:23013:0:7:283:290:564:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:(
10:332:23014:7:16:302:308:557:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:1

10:334:23018:0:0:321:339:549:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f8:−ρ
10:335:23020:0:15:339:346:564:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:)

10:337:23026:26:18:72:540:523:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Note thatbis positive because 0< θ <1 and|ρ|<1. In other words, a fund’s optimally
10:338:23108:18:45:72:519:505:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:chosen turnover exhibits a positive time-series relation to the fund’s subsequent return.
10:339:23197:45:36:72:342:460:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2.4  Time-Series versus Cross-Section
10:340:23234:36:18:72:539:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Most studies investigating the relation between fund turnover and performance focus on
10:341:23320:18:18:72:540:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the cross-section. The question generally asked is whether there is a relation, across funds,
10:342:23413:18:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between average turnover and average return. Taking the unconditional expectation of the
10:343:23501:18:30:72:446:370:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time-series relation in equation (11), using equations (12) and (13), gives
10:344:23576:30:30:259:540:340:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:E(Rt) =hE(X∗t),(14)
10:345:23595:30:19:72:102:310:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where
10:346:23600:19:0:266:293:291:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:h=c
10:347:23603:0:10:295:303:309:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:(
10:348:23604:10:16:315:320:299:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:θ
10:349:23605:16:0:305:330:283:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:1−θ
10:350:23608:0:18:332:340:309:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:)
10:351:23609:18:28:342:540:291:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:.(15)
10:352:23614:28:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Ifcandθare the same across funds, thenhis the same for each fund. In that case, equation
10:353:23702:18:17:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(14) represents the relation between average turnover and average performance across funds.
10:354:23793:17:18:72:539:228:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:From equation (5) we see that funds typically experiencing higher values ofπt, and thus
10:355:23880:18:18:72:539:210:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:greater profit opportunities, trade more and thus have higher values of E(X∗t). From (14),
10:356:23970:18:18:72:540:192:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this higher average turnover is accompanied by higher return, because the slope in the cross-
10:357:24063:18:18:72:540:174:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sectional relation,h, is positive (recalling 0< θ <1). However, this cross-sectional slope is
10:358:24156:18:30:72:539:156:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lower than the slope of the time-series relation,b. Specifically, from equations (13) and (15),
10:359:24251:30:30:261:540:126:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:b−h=c(1−ρ),(16)
10:360:24266:30:18:72:540:96:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which is positive.  The time-series slope is greater because trading costs associated with
10:361:24356:18:0:72:540:78:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover do not subtract from the fund’s return in the same period as the profit resulting
11:362:24447:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from that turnover. In contrast, the timing of profit and trading cost is irrelevant for the
11:363:24539:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cross-sectional relation. Trading costs therefore weaken the time-series turnover-performance
11:364:24632:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relation by less than they weaken the cross-sectional relation. The empirical results in the
11:365:24724:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:next section are consistent with the model’s implied difference between the time-series and
11:366:24815:18:43:72:302:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cross-sectional slopes, given in equation (16).
11:367:24862:43:37:72:503:608:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:3.  Estimating the Turnover-Performance Relation
11:368:24910:37:18:72:540:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Following equation (11), we specify the time-series turnover-performance relation for a given
11:369:25003:18:30:72:223:553:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fundias the linear regression
11:370:25032:30:30:240:540:523:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Ri,t=ai+biXi,t−1+-i,t,(17)
11:371:25058:30:18:72:540:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereRi,tis the fund’s benchmark-adjusted return in periodt, andXi,t−1is the fund’s
11:372:25141:18:18:72:539:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover in periodt−1. As implied by our model, a positivebireflects the fund’s skill to
11:373:25229:18:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:identify and trade on opportunities in periodt−1 for which a significant portion of the payoff
11:374:25323:18:18:72:539:439:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:occurs in periodt. One can imagine other forms of skill, outside of the model, that we would
11:375:25415:18:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not detect. For example, a fund could have skill to identify short-horizon opportunities,
11:376:25504:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:such as liquidity provision, that deliver all of their profits in periodt−1.7Or a fund could
11:377:25596:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:identify only long-horizon opportunities that bear fruit after periodt. Moreover, detecting
11:378:25687:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:skill using the turnover-performance relation requires time variation in the extent to which
11:379:25779:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:profit opportunities arise, i.e., variation inπtin equation (1). Although the regression in
11:380:25870:18:17:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equation (17) cannot detect all forms of skill, it nevertheless provides novel insights into the
11:381:25966:17:29:72:443:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ability of funds to identify and exploit time-varying profit opportunities.
11:382:26041:29:18:89:539:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We explore the turnover-performance relation using the dataset constructed by P ́astor,
11:383:26128:18:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Stambaugh, and Taylor (2015), who combine CRSP and Morningstar data to obtain a sample
11:384:26214:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of 3,126 actively managed U.S. domestic equity mutual funds covering the 1979–2011 period.
11:385:26304:18:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To measure the dependent variableRi,t, we follow the above study in usingGrossRi,t, the
11:386:26391:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s net return minus the return on the benchmark index designated by Morningstar, plus
11:387:26480:18:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the fund’s monthly expense ratio taken from CRSP. Following our model, we use gross return,
11:388:26571:18:18:72:540:177:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:i.e., the return before fees charged to investors. We estimate all regressions at a monthly
11:389:26662:18:18:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:frequency, but a fund’s turnover is reported only as the total for its fiscal year. Thus, we
11:390:26754:18:18:72:540:141:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measure turnover,Xi,t−1, by the variableF undT urni,t−1, which is the fund’s turnover for
11:391:26843:18:16:85:540:123:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:7In the presence of skill, a higherXi,t−1can contribute positively to bothRi,t−1andRi,t. Thus, one might
11:392:26947:16:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:also look for a positive contemporaneous relation between turnover and return. Such a relation, however,
11:393:27051:12:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:could simply reflect a manager’s trading in reaction to return, thereby confounding an inference about skill.
11:394:27160:12:0:72:440:83:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:We therefore focus on the predictive turnover-performance relation in equation (17).
12:395:27245:0:29:72:481:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the most recent fiscal year that ends before montht. This measure is defined as
12:396:27324:29:0:194:282:694:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:F undT urni,t−1=
12:397:27340:0:16:287:410:702:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:min (buysi,t−1, sellsi,t−1)
12:398:27367:16:0:310:387:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:avg (T NAi,t−1)
12:399:27382:0:30:414:540:694:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:,(18)
12:400:27387:30:18:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where the numerator is the lesser of the fund’s total purchases and sales over its most recent
12:401:27481:18:18:72:540:646:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fiscal year that ends before montht, and the denominator is the fund’s average total net
12:402:27569:18:18:72:540:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:asset value over the same 12-month period. We have no discretion over this definition; this
12:403:27660:18:17:72:540:610:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is the measure of turnover that funds are required to report to the SEC, and it is also the
12:404:27751:17:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measure provided by CRSP. We discuss some properties of this measure later in Section
12:405:27836:18:29:72:416:575:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:3.2.1. We winsorizeF undT urni,t−1at the 1st and 99th percentiles.
12:406:27902:29:18:89:540:546:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To increase the power of our inferences in equation (17), we estimate a panel regression
12:407:27990:18:18:72:214:528:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that imposes the restriction
12:408:28018:18:23:259:540:510:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:b1=b2=···=b .(19)
12:409:28035:23:18:72:540:487:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Initially we pool across all funds, and then later we pool within various fund categories when
12:410:28129:18:18:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:investigating heterogeneity in the turnover-performance relation. We include fund fixed ef-
12:411:28220:18:18:72:539:451:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fects, so thatbreflects only the contribution of within-fund time variation in turnover. The
12:412:28312:18:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund fixed effects correspond to theai’s in equation (17) when the restriction in (19) is im-
12:413:28405:18:18:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:posed across all funds. The regression specification combining equations (17) and (19), which
12:414:28498:18:18:72:540:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:isolates the time-series relation between turnover and performance, is our main specification.
12:415:28592:18:45:72:447:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For comparison, we also consider other specifications, as we explain next.
12:416:28666:45:36:72:417:334:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.1.  Time-series versus cross-sectional estimates
12:417:28716:36:18:72:540:298:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Table 1 reports the estimated slope coefficient on turnover, or̂b,for various specifications of
12:418:28811:18:18:72:539:280:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:the panel regression capturing the turnover-performance relation. The top left cell reportŝb
12:419:28904:18:27:72:427:262:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from our main specification, which combines equations (17) and (19):
12:420:28972:27:26:242:540:235:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Ri,t=ai+bXi,t−1+-i,t.(20)
12:421:28997:26:18:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This specification includes fund fixed effects, so the OLS estimatêbreflects only time-series
12:422:29091:18:18:72:540:191:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:variation in turnover and performance. This statement emerges clearly from the fact that,
12:423:29180:18:18:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with fund fixed effects,̂bis a weighted average across funds of the slope estimates from
12:424:29268:18:18:72:540:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund-by-fund time-series regressions.  The weighting scheme places larger weights on the
12:425:29356:18:18:72:540:137:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:time-series slopes of funds with more observations as well as funds whose turnover fluctuates
12:426:29449:18:29:72:307:119:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more over time. See the Appendix for details.
12:427:29494:29:18:89:539:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The estimatêbin the top left cell of Table 1 is positive and highly significant, with a
12:428:29582:18:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:t-statistic of 6.63. This finding of a positive turnover-performance relation in the time series
13:429:29680:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is the main empirical result of the paper. The relation is significant not only statistically but
13:430:29777:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:also economically. The average within-fund standard deviation ofXi,t−1is 0.438. Therefore,
13:431:29867:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the estimated slope of 0.00123 implies that a one-standard-deviation increase in a fund’s
13:432:29956:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f11:turnover translates to an increase in annualized expected return of 0.65% (= 0.00123×
13:433:30041:18:18:72:539:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:0.438×1200). This number is substantial, in that it is comparable in magnitude to funds’
13:434:30129:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:overall average annualizedRi,t, equal to 0.60%. In other words, conditioning fund returns
13:435:30218:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on turnover implies fluctuations in the conditional expected return that are of first-order
13:436:30309:18:28:72:452:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:economic importance, often as large as the unconditional expected return.
13:437:30382:28:18:89:539:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The top right cell of Table 1 reportŝbfrom a panel regression that includes both fund
13:438:30468:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and month fixed effects. The resulting estimate, 0.00106, is only slightly smaller than its
13:439:30559:18:18:72:539:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:counterpart in the top left cell, and it is similarly significant (t= 6.77). The only differ-
13:440:30652:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ence from the top left cell is the addition of month fixed effects. This addition controls for
13:441:30746:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:any unobserved variables that change over time but not across funds, such as macroeco-
13:442:30832:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nomic variables, regulatory changes, and aggregate trading activity. Since the results with
13:443:30923:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and without month fixed effects are so similar, such aggregate variables cannot explain the
13:444:31014:18:29:72:340:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:positive relation between turnover and performance.
13:445:31065:29:18:89:539:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The bottom left cell reportŝbwhen no fixed effects are included in the panel regression.
13:446:31154:18:24:72:398:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:This specification imposes not only the restriction (19) but also
13:447:31219:24:24:258:540:372:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:a1=a2=···=a .(21)
13:448:31236:24:18:72:540:348:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:By removing fund fixed effects from our main specification, this additional restriction brings
13:449:31330:18:18:72:540:330:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cross-sectional variation into play when estimatingb.  The estimatêbin the bottom left
13:450:31417:18:18:72:540:312:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cell of Table 1 thus reflects both cross-sectional and time-series variation. This estimate is
13:451:31511:18:29:72:454:294:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:positive, 0.00040, but only marginally significant, with at-statistic of 1.92.
13:452:31589:29:18:89:540:265:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The bottom right cell of Table 1 reportŝbfrom a purely cross-sectional specification, in
13:453:31678:18:25:72:405:247:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which fund fixed effectsaiare replaced by month fixed effectsat:
13:454:31742:25:24:242:540:222:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Ri,t=at+bXi,t−1+-i,t.(22)
13:455:31767:24:18:72:539:198:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The OLS estimatêbfrom this panel regression reflects only cross-sectional variation in
13:456:31854:18:18:72:539:180:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:turnover and performance.  To see this, note that including month fixed effects makeŝb
13:457:31941:18:18:72:540:162:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:equal to a weighted average across periods of the slope estimates from period-by-period
13:458:32028:18:18:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cross-sectional regressions of performance on turnover. The weighting scheme places larger
13:459:32118:18:18:72:540:126:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:weights on periods with more observations and periods in which the independent variable ex-
13:460:32209:18:18:72:540:108:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:hibits more cross-sectional variance. If each period receives the same weight, then this panel
13:461:32303:18:18:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:regression produces the same slope coefficient as the well known Fama-Macbeth (1973) esti-
13:462:32393:18:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mator. (See the Appendix.) The estimate ofbfrom equation (22), 0.00030, is positive but the
14:463:32486:0:18:72:539:723:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:t-statistic is only 1.61. The point estimate is smaller than in the bottom left cell, which shows
14:464:32583:18:29:72:532:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that isolating cross-sectional variation further weakens the turnover-performance relation.
14:465:32674:29:18:89:540:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Table 1 clearly shows that the turnover-performance relation is stronger in the time
14:466:32758:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:series than in the cross section. Recall from our model that we expect such a result, with
14:467:32848:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the difference between the time-series and cross-sectional slopes given by equation (16). In
14:468:32940:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fact, the difference between these slopes in Table 1 is roughly in line with equation (16),
14:469:33031:17:18:72:539:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:given estimates ofρandc. Forρ, we take the average autocorrelation ofF undT urni,t−1,
14:470:33116:18:18:72:539:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which is equal to 0.507. Forc, we turn to Edelen, Evans, and Kadlec (2013), who report
14:471:33202:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that, on average, the equity mutual funds in their sample have annual turnover of 82.4%
14:472:33289:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and incur 1.44% of fund value annually in trading costs.  The implied value ofcis then
14:473:33375:18:18:72:539:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:0.0144/0.824 = 0.0175.  From equation (16), the difference between the time-series and
14:474:33461:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:cross-sectional slopes is then equal toc(1−ρ) = 0.0175(1−0.507) = 0.0086. Given thatρ
14:475:33546:18:18:72:539:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:andcare annual quantities, this value is the implied difference in slopes when annual return
14:476:33638:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is regressed on annual turnover. Table 1 instead reports slopes for monthly return regressed
14:477:33730:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on 12-month turnover. Multiplying the latter slopes by 12 puts them roughly on a 12-month
14:478:33819:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:basis. Subtracting the cross-sectional slope in the lower-right cell of Table 1 from the time-
14:479:33913:18:18:72:539:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:series slope in the upper-left cell, multiplying by 12, gives 12(0.00123−0.00030) = 0.0112,
14:480:34004:18:29:72:430:407:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:which rounds to 0.01, just like the above implied difference of 0.0086.8
14:481:34076:29:18:89:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In sum, consistent with our model in which fund managers identify and exploit time-
14:482:34159:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:varying profit opportunities, a fund’s performance exhibits a highly significant positive rela-
14:483:34254:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tion to its lagged turnover. As our model also predicts, this time-series relation is stronger
14:484:34348:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than the weakly positive cross-sectional relation between turnover and performance. More-
14:485:34437:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:over, the magnitude of the difference between the time-series and cross-sectional slopes con-
14:486:34530:18:46:72:197:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:forms well to our model.
14:487:34554:46:36:72:189:243:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3.2.  Robustness
14:488:34570:36:18:72:540:207:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The positive turnover-performance relation documented above, which is our main result, is
14:489:34659:18:18:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:robust to a variety of specification changes. We summarize the robustness results here and
14:490:34749:18:29:72:482:171:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:report them in detail in the online appendix, which is available on our websites.
14:491:34830:29:18:89:539:142:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We have already shown that the turnover-performance relation obtains whether or not
14:492:34913:18:17:72:540:124:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:month fixed effects are included in the panel regression, which rules out all aggregate variables
14:493:35010:17:16:85:540:107:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:8The time-series and cross-sectional slopes when 12-month return is regressed on 12-month turnover equal
14:494:35114:16:12:72:540:91:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:0.0200 and 0.0107, as reported in the online appendix. The difference in these slopes, 0.0093, is also quite
14:495:35222:12:0:72:276:79:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:close to the above implied difference of 0.0086.
15:496:35272:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as the source of this relation. Furthermore, the relation obtains when we include benchmark-
15:497:35364:18:18:72:539:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:month fixed effects, ruling out any variables measured at the benchmark-month level.9An
15:498:35451:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:example of such a variable is benchmark turnover, which can be reflected in a fund’s turnover
15:499:35544:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to the extent that some of the fund’s trading passively responds to reconstitutions of the
15:500:35634:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s benchmark index. Adding benchmark-month fixed effects has a tiny effect on the
15:501:35719:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:estimated turnover-performance relation, strengthening our interpretation of this relation as
15:502:35812:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:being driven by skilled active trading. The relation also obtains, and is equally strong, when
15:503:35906:18:28:72:311:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gross fund returns are replaced by net returns.
15:504:35953:28:18:89:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Importantly, the positive turnover-performance relation doesnotobtain in a placebo test
15:505:36040:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in which we replace active funds by passive index funds, as identified by Morningstar. When
15:506:36131:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we produce the counterpart of Table 1 for the universe of passive funds, we find no slope
15:507:36220:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:coefficient significantly different from zero. In fact, the estimated slope coefficients in the
15:508:36315:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:specifications with fund fixed effects are not even positive (the correspondingt-statistics in
15:509:36409:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the top row of Table 1 are -0.51 and -1.07). This result is comforting because passive funds
15:510:36501:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:should not exhibit any skill in identifying time-varying profit opportunities. The fact that
15:511:36593:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the turnover-performance relation emerges for active funds but not passive funds supports
15:512:36682:18:29:72:303:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our skill-based interpretation of this relation.
15:513:36730:29:18:89:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:If a fund’s turnover is negatively correlated with the fund’s contemporaneous or lagged
15:514:36817:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:return, then a finite sample tends to produce a positive sample correlation between return
15:515:36907:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and lagged turnover even if this correlation’s true value is zero. This bias, essentially the same
15:516:37005:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as analyzed by Stambaugh (1999), arises because the sample’s relatively high (low) turnover
15:517:37096:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:values tend to be accompanied by the sample’s low (high) current and past returns. Those
15:518:37184:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:high (low) turnover values thus tend to precede the sample’s relatively high (low) returns,
15:519:37275:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thereby producing an apparent positive relation between return and lagged turnover. We
15:520:37361:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:find that the correlations between turnover and both contemporaneous and lagged return
15:521:37447:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are negative but statistically insignificant. We nevertheless conduct a simulation analysis to
15:522:37541:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gauge the potential magnitude of the bias as well as the effectiveness of a simple remedy in
15:523:37633:18:18:72:539:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our setting—addingRi,t−1andRi,t−2as independent variables to the regression in equation
15:524:37720:18:18:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(20). The simulation reveals that the finite-sample bias is very small and that adding the
15:525:37810:18:18:72:539:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lagged returns is nevertheless effective in eliminating it. When we addRi,t−1andRi,t−2to
15:526:37898:18:28:72:539:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the regression in (20), the resulting slope onXi,t−1and itst-statistic are virtually unchanged.
15:527:37993:28:18:89:539:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We estimate the turnover-performance relation at the monthly frequency. Even though
15:528:38076:18:18:72:540:117:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds report their turnover only annually, most of the variables used in our subsequent
15:529:38163:18:16:85:540:99:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:9Gormley and Matsa (2014), among others, advocate the use of a fixed-effects estimator as a way of
15:530:38261:16:0:72:379:83:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:controlling for unobserved group heterogeneity in finance applications.
16:531:38334:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:analysis, such as fund returns, fund size, industry size, sentiment, volatility, liquidity, and
16:532:38429:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:business-cycle indicators, are available on a monthly basis. Therefore, we choose the monthly
16:533:38522:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:frequency in an effort to utilize all available information. Nonetheless, when we reestimate
16:534:38614:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the turnover-performance relation by using annual fund returns, we find a positive and highly
16:535:38707:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significant time-series relation, just like in Table 1. In addition, we consider a specification
16:536:38803:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that allows the slope coefficient from the monthly turnover-performance regression to depend
16:537:38895:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:on the number of months between the end of the 12-month period over whichF undT urn
16:538:38978:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is measured and the month in which the fund return is computed. Specifically, we add a
16:539:39064:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:term to the right-hand side of the regression that interacts the above number of months with
16:540:39156:18:17:72:539:561:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:F undT urn. We find that the interaction term does not enter significantly, suggesting that
16:541:39247:17:29:72:310:544:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our constant-slope specification is appropriate.
16:542:39295:29:18:89:539:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To judge the statistical significance of the turnover-performance slope estimates in the
16:543:39383:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:presence of fund fixed effects, we compute standard errors clustered by sector times month,
16:544:39474:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:where sector denotes a Morningstar style category. We choose this approach because there is
16:545:39565:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mild correlation between benchmark-adjusted fund returns within the same sector but very
16:546:39653:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:little across sectors. For robustness, we also consider stricter clustering schemes, namely, by
16:547:39748:18:29:72:449:425:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:month, and by fund and month, and continue to find significant results.10
16:548:39821:29:18:89:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our turnover-performance relation captures the predictive power ofF undT urnin a given
16:549:39907:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fiscal year for fund performance in the following fiscal year (e.g., turnover in 2014 predicts
16:550:40001:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:returns in 2015). In principle, some fund trades could take longer to play out (e.g., a trade in
16:551:40097:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:2014 could lead to profits in 2016).11To test for such long-horizon effects, we add two more
16:552:40189:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:lags ofF undT urnto the right-hand side of regression (20). We find that neither of those
16:553:40278:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:additional lags has any predictive power for returns after controlling for the most recent
16:554:40368:18:18:72:539:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:value ofF undT urn, which retains its positive and significant coefficient. Therefore, we use
16:555:40461:18:29:72:375:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:only the most recentF undT urnin the rest of our analysis.
16:556:40519:29:18:89:540:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our results are not driven by manager changes. When we replace fund fixed effects by
16:557:40603:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund-manager fixed effects, the results are very similar. The turnover-performance relation
16:558:40694:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thus holds not only at the fund level but also at the manager level. One implication is that
16:559:40786:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our results are not driven by portfolio turnover during manager transitions. In addition, our
16:560:40879:18:17:72:497:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:results easily survive the addition of controls for manager age and manager tenure.
16:561:40962:17:16:81:540:153:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:10In turnover-performance regressions that exclude fund fixed effects, we cluster not only by sector times
16:562:41068:16:12:72:540:137:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:month but also by fund, to account for potential residual correlation induced by the exclusion of fund fixed
16:563:41176:12:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:effects.  In subsequent regressions withF undT urnas the dependent variable, we cluster by fund, since
16:564:41278:12:8:72:489:113:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f7:F undT urnis highly persistent, and by year, to allow cross-sectional dependence inF undT urn.
16:565:41372:8:16:81:540:105:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:11The relations between fund performance and funds’ investment horizons are analyzed by Yan and Zhang
16:566:41473:16:0:72:468:89:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:(2009), Cremers and Pareek (2016), and Lan, Moneta, and Wermers (2015), among others.
17:567:41560:0:18:89:539:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We run a linear turnover-performance regression.  Besides its natural simplicity, the
17:568:41645:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:linear specification is motivated by our model. Recall that if the trading cost function is
17:569:41736:18:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:approximately linear (γ≈0), so is the turnover-performance relation (see equation (11)).
17:570:41824:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In principle, the relation could also be convex (ifγ  >0), but we find no such evidence.
17:571:41912:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We estimate a nonparametric regression ofRi,tonXi,t−1, both demeaned at the fund level.
17:572:41999:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We find that the fitted values from that regression are remarkably close to linear, providing
17:573:42092:18:28:72:360:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:support for our regression specification in equation (20).
17:574:42150:28:18:89:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The positive turnover-performance relation emerges not only from the panel regression
17:575:42235:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in Table 1, which imposes the restriction (19), but also from fund-by-fund regressions. For
17:576:42326:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:each fundi, we estimate the slopebifrom the time-series regression in equation (17) in the
17:577:42416:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:full sample. We find that 61% of the OLS slope estimateŝbiare positive. Moreover, 9% (4%)
17:578:42506:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of thêbi’s are significantly positive at the 5% (1%) confidence level. A weighted average of
17:579:42599:18:18:72:539:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thesêbi’s appears in the top left cell of Table 1, as shown in equation (37).12Apart from
17:580:42689:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this brief summary, we do not analyze thêbiestimates because their precision is generally
17:581:42779:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:low given the funds’ relatively short track records. Instead, we focus on the panel-regression
17:582:42873:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:estimate ofbwhose precision is higher thanks to information-pooling across funds. The panel-
17:583:42965:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:regression slope characterizes the typical fund-month observation, rather than the typical
17:584:43055:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund. Therefore, we do not find that the typical fund exhibits a positive turnover-performance
17:585:43149:18:18:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relation. Rather, we find that the typical fund-month exhibits a positive relation, which
17:586:43238:18:28:72:445:371:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:implies that there must exist some funds that exhibit a positive relation.
17:587:43312:28:18:89:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Mutual funds sometimes benefit from receiving allocations of shares in initial public
17:588:43397:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:offerings (IPOs) at below-market prices. Lead underwriters tend to allocate more IPO shares
17:589:43488:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to fund families from which they receive larger brokerage commissions (e.g., Reuter, 2006).
17:590:43579:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To the extent that higher commissions are associated with higher turnover, this practice
17:591:43667:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:could potentially contribute to a positive turnover-performance relation. This contribution
17:592:43758:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is unlikely to be substantial, though. Fund families tend to distribute IPO shares across
17:593:43847:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds based on criteria such as past returns and fees rather than turnover (Gaspar, Massa,
17:594:43937:18:18:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and Matos, 2006). In addition, the high commissions that help families earn IPO allocations
17:595:44028:18:18:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:often reflect an elevated commission rate rather than high family turnover, and they are often
17:596:44122:18:18:72:539:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:paid around the time of the IPO rather than over the previous fiscal year.13Moreover, the
17:597:44211:18:18:72:540:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:contribution of IPO allocations to fund performance seems modest. For each year between
17:598:44298:18:18:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:1980 and 2013, we calculate the ratio of total money left on the table across all IPOs, obtained
17:599:44394:18:19:72:540:127:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from Jay Ritter’s website, to total assets of active domestic equity mutual funds, obtained
17:600:44485:19:15:81:540:108:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:12The cross-sectional correlation between̂biand the length of fundi’s track record is insignificant at 0.02,
17:601:44593:15:9:72:449:93:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:indicating that the turnover-performance relation is no stronger for longer-lived funds.
17:602:44681:9:0:81:528:84:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:13See, for example, Nimalendran, Ritter, and Zhang (2007) and Goldstein, Irvine, and Puckett (2011).
18:603:44783:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from the Investment Company Institute.  This ratio, whose mean is 0.30%, exceeds the
18:604:44867:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:contribution of IPO allocations to fund performance because mutual funds receive only about
18:605:44958:18:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:25% to 41% of IPO allocations, on average.14IPOs thus boost average fund performance
18:606:45042:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by only about 7.5 to 12 basis points per year. Furthermore, the IPO market has cooled
18:607:45127:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significantly since year 2000. Money left on the table has decreased to only 0.10% of fund
18:608:45217:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assets on average, so that IPOs have boosted average fund performance by only 2.5 to 4
18:609:45303:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:basis points per year since January 2001. Yet the turnover-performance relation remains
18:610:45390:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:strong during this cold-IPO-market subperiod: the slope estimates in the top row of Table
18:611:45479:18:28:72:409:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:1 remain positive and significant, witht-statistics in excess of 3.2.
18:612:45548:28:18:89:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:If we were to redefine our dependent variable from fund returns to dollar value added
18:613:45633:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(Berk and van Binsbergen, 2015), the results would be very similar, by the following logic.
18:614:45724:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:When the dependent variable is dollar value added, the independent variable should be
18:615:45809:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover in dollars. Making these changes amounts to multiplying both sides of our cur-
18:616:45896:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rent regression by fund size. The new regression suffers from a heteroskedasticity problem,
18:617:45987:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:because larger funds have more-volatile (dollar) residuals. Adjusting for this heteroskedas-
18:618:46079:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ticity requires down-weighting larger funds, for example, by dividing both sides of the new
18:619:46170:18:29:72:489:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:regression by fund size. After this division, we are back to our current regression.
18:620:46254:29:18:89:539:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We report all of our results based on the full sample period of 1979–2011. In addition, we
18:621:46344:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:verify the robustness of our results in the 2000–2011 subperiod, motivated by two potential
18:622:46435:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:structural changes in the data. The first change relates to the way CRSP reports turnover.
18:623:46525:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Prior to September 1998, all funds’ fiscal years are reported as January–December, raising
18:624:46615:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the possibility of inaccuracy, since after 1998 the timing of funds’ fiscal years varies across
18:625:46710:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds.15The second change, identified by P ́astor, Stambaugh, and Taylor (2015), relates to
18:626:46801:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the reporting of fund size and expense ratios before 1993. Using the 2000–2011 subperiod
18:627:46889:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:provides a robustness check that is conservative in avoiding both potential structural changes.
18:628:46984:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We find that all of our main conclusions are robust to using the 2000–2011 subperiod.
18:629:47069:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For example, the time-series turnover-performance relation in Table 1 remains positive and
18:630:47159:18:18:72:539:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significant, witht-statistics of 4.37 and 3.74 in the top row.  In the online appendix, we
18:631:47249:18:18:72:490:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:report the counterparts of all of our tables estimated in the 2000–2011 subperiod.
18:632:47331:18:12:81:508:181:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:14These estimates are from Reuter (2006), Ritter and Zhang (2007), and Field and Lowry (2009).
18:633:47425:12:15:81:540:169:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:15In private communication, CRSP explained that this change in reporting is related to the change in its
18:634:47529:15:12:72:540:154:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:fund data provider from S&P to Lipper on August 31, 1998. CRSP has also explained the timing convention
18:635:47632:12:12:72:539:142:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:for turnover, which is the variableturnratioin CRSP’sfundfeesfile. If the variablefiscalyearendis present
18:636:47737:12:12:72:540:130:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:in the file, turnover is measured over the 12-month period ending on thefiscalyearenddate; otherwise
18:637:47837:12:0:72:493:118:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:turnover is measured over the 12-month period ending on the date marked by the variablebegdt.
19:638:47932:0:37:72:232:723:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.2.1.  Measuring Turnover
19:639:47958:37:18:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We measure fund turnover by its official SEC definition from equation (18). One advantage
19:640:48047:18:17:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of this measure is that, by taking the minimum of purchases and sales, it largely excludes
19:641:48137:17:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover arising from persistent inflows and outflows to and from the fund. For example,
19:642:48225:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:if a fund experiences inflows throughout the year, it will probably use those inflows to buy
19:643:48317:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stocks, but the SEC turnover will pick up the fund’s sales, which are not driven by flows.
19:644:48407:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Similarly, if a fund experiences persistent outflows, there will be flow-driven selling, but our
19:645:48503:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover measure will pick up the fund’s purchases. Since fund flows are well known to be
19:646:48592:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:persistent, our turnover measure is largely immune to flows. Instead, it reflects mostly the
19:647:48684:18:29:72:428:543:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund’s active portfolio decisions to replace some holdings with others.
19:648:48755:29:18:89:539:514:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our turnover measure is not completely immune to fund flows, though. If flows are non-
19:649:48841:18:18:72:540:496:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:persistent then some of our turnover is flow-driven. Flow-driven trading is fairly mechanical
19:650:48934:18:18:72:540:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in that its timing is determined mostly by the fund’s investors rather than the fund’s man-
19:651:49025:18:17:72:540:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ager. Therefore, flow-driven turnover should exhibit a weaker relation to fund performance
19:652:49115:17:18:72:539:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:than our turnover measure,F undT urn.  To test this hypothesis, we construct two mea-
19:653:49200:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sures of flow-driven fund turnover. Both measures rely on monthly dollar flows, which we
19:654:49288:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:back out from the monthly series of fund size and fund returns, and both cover the same
19:655:49375:18:18:72:539:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:12-month period asF undT urn. The first measure is the sum of the absolute values of the
19:656:49463:18:18:72:540:371:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:12 monthly dollar flows, divided by the average fund size during the 12-month period. The
19:657:49552:18:18:72:540:353:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:second measure is the smaller of two sums, one of all positive dollar flows and one of all neg-
19:658:49647:18:18:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ative flows during the 12-month period, divided by average fund size. Consistent with our
19:659:49736:18:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:hypothesis, we find that neither measure of flow-driven turnover has any predictive power for
19:660:49829:18:18:72:539:299:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund returns, whether or not we includeF undT urnas a control. Moreover, the inclusion of
19:661:49918:18:18:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:flow-driven turnover does not affect the significant predictive power ofF undT urn. Finally,
19:662:50010:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when we adjust our turnover measure for flows by subtracting flow-driven turnover from
19:663:50096:18:18:72:539:245:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:F undT urn, we find that the difference strongly predicts fund performance. All these results
19:664:50189:18:29:72:524:227:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:provide additional support for our interpretation of the turnover-performance relation.16
19:665:50278:29:17:89:540:198:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In our final test related to fund flows, we calculate their time-series volatility, which could
19:666:50373:17:18:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in principle be related to the time variation in fund turnover. We compute flow volatility
19:667:50463:18:18:72:540:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for each fund as the standard deviation of the fund’s 12 monthly net flows during the same
19:668:50553:18:18:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:period over whichF undT urnis measured. When we add flow volatility as a control in our
19:669:50640:18:18:72:540:127:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover-performance regression, the control does not enter significantly and the slope on
19:670:50730:18:18:72:353:109:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:F undT urnremains very similar and highly significant.
19:671:50784:18:15:81:540:91:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:16Our results are also broadly consistent with those of Alexander, Cici, and Gibson (2007) who find that
