19:672:50888:15:0:72:461:76:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:future returns of funds’ discretionary trades are higher than those of flow-induced trades.
20:673:50981:0:18:89:539:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In addition to fund flows, some portion of turnover could be driven by other non-
20:674:51062:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:discretionary forces such as manager transitions, benchmark index reconstitutions, portfolio
20:675:51154:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rebalancing, etc. Turnover driven by manager transitions cannot explain our results because
20:676:51245:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:those hold up when we replace fund fixed effects by manager fixed effects, as noted earlier.
20:677:51337:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Benchmark index reconstitutions cannot explain our results either because those survive the
20:678:51428:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inclusion of benchmark-month fixed effects, as explained earlier. Another way to account
20:679:51516:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for benchmark index turnover is to estimate it from the turnover of index funds tracking
20:680:51604:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the fund’s benchmark. For each active fund, we calculate benchmark-adjusted turnover as
20:681:51691:18:18:72:539:579:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:F undT urnminus the median turnover of all index funds in the same Morningstar cate-
20:682:51775:18:17:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gory, measured over the same period asF undT urn. When we replaceF undT urnby its
20:683:51856:17:18:72:540:544:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:benchmark-adjusted version, we continue to find a positive and highly significant turnover-
20:684:51947:18:29:72:181:526:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance relation.
20:685:51968:29:18:89:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Regardless of its source, any trading unrelated to profit motive widens the gap between
20:686:52055:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a fund’s turnover and its optimal turnover in the context of our model.  Therefore, any
20:687:52142:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:such trading should make it more difficult for us to find a positive turnover-performance
20:688:52231:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relation.  Yet we do find a strong relation, even without adjusting reported turnover for
20:689:52320:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:non-discretionary trading. It is possible that some adjustment could enhance the predictive
20:690:52411:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:power of SEC turnover, but it is not our goal to find the best predictor of fund returns. For
20:691:52504:18:29:72:459:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:simplicity, we use the SEC turnover measure throughout our main analysis.
20:692:52577:29:17:89:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For robustness, we consider one more modification of our turnover measure. The denom-
20:693:52662:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inator of our measure is average fund size over the previous fiscal year. To see whether this
20:694:52755:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:averaging somehow influences our results, we rescale our turnover measure by the ratio of
20:695:52844:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the same average fund size to fund size at the beginning of the previous fiscal year. The
20:696:52933:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:denominator of the turnover measure thus changes from average size to fund size at the
20:697:53019:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:beginning of the previous fiscal year. We find that this rescaled turnover measure predicts
20:698:53110:18:29:72:409:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance even more strongly than our standard SEC measure.
20:699:53171:29:18:89:539:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Even though we analyze equity mutual funds, some of the funds’ turnover could be due
20:700:53255:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to non-equity assets.  To see whether non-equity turnover matters, we obtain data from
20:701:53341:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Morningstar on the percentage of each fund’s assets invested in stock. When we add this
20:702:53428:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:percentage as a control in our turnover-performance regression, it enters with a small positive
20:703:53523:18:0:72:460:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:coefficient, but the explanatory power ofF undT urnis virtually unchanged.
21:704:53599:0:37:72:298:723:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.2.2.  Alternative Benchmark Models
21:705:53635:37:18:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We benchmark each fund’s performance against the index selected for the fund’s category
21:706:53722:18:17:72:540:668:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by Morningstar. For example, for small-cap value funds, the benchmark is the Russell 2000
21:707:53811:17:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Value Index; for large-cap growth funds, it is Russell 1000 Growth.  Morningstar assigns
21:708:53899:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds to categories by relying heavily on the funds’ reported portfolio holdings. Since these
21:709:53992:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assignments are made by Morningstar rather than by funds themselves, there is no room
21:710:54077:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for benchmark manipulation of the kind documented by Sensoy (2009).  The benchmark
21:711:54159:18:29:72:479:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:assigned by Morningstar can differ from that reported in the fund’s prospectus.
21:712:54238:29:18:89:539:550:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our index-based approach is likely to adjust for fund style and risk more precisely than
21:713:54326:18:18:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the commonly used loadings on the three Fama-French factors. The Fama-French factors
21:714:54410:18:18:72:540:514:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are popular in mutual fund studies because their returns are freely available, unlike the
21:715:54499:18:18:72:540:496:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Morningstar benchmark index data. Yet the Fama-French factors are not obvious benchmark
21:716:54586:18:18:72:540:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:choices because they are long-short portfolios whose returns cannot be costlessly achieved by
21:717:54679:18:17:72:540:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mutual fund managers. Moreover, Cremers, Petajisto, and Zitzewitz (2013) argue that the
21:718:54766:17:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Fama-French model produces biased assessments of fund performance, and they recommend
21:719:54851:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:using index-based benchmarks instead. We follow this advice. But we find similar results
21:720:54939:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:when we adjust fund returns by using the three Fama-French factors: the slope coefficients in
21:721:55032:18:18:72:539:389:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the top row of Table 1 continue to be highly significant, witht-statistics of 7.09 and 8.27, while
21:722:55130:18:18:72:540:371:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the slopes in the bottom row remain insignificant. We also find similar results when using
21:723:55220:18:18:72:540:353:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:three additional alternative benchmark models: the four-factor model that includes the three
21:724:55312:18:18:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Fama-French factors and momentum, the five-factor model of Fama and French (2014), and
21:725:55398:18:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the modified Fama-French three-factor model of Cremers, Petajisto, and Zitzewitz (2013).
21:726:55486:18:18:72:540:299:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In all three cases, our main slope coefficients in the top row of Table 1 continue to be highly
21:727:55581:18:18:72:539:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significant, witht-statistics ranging from 5.93 to 9.34. The slope coefficients in the bottom
21:728:55674:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:row remain insignificant, except when we use the Fama-French five factors or Cremers-
21:729:55759:18:18:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Petajisto-Zitzewitz factors, for which thet-statistics range from 2.05 to 3.71. That is, under
21:730:55853:18:18:72:540:227:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:those two benchmark models, the positive turnover-performance relation emerges also from
21:731:55941:18:28:72:465:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the cross-section, but in general, the relation appears only in the time series.
21:732:56021:28:18:89:540:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We assess fund performance by subtracting Morningstar’s designated benchmark return
21:733:56104:18:18:72:540:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from the fund’s return, effectively assuming that the fund’s benchmark beta is equal to
21:734:56191:18:18:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:one. This simple approach is popular in investment practice, and it circumvents the need to
21:735:56282:18:18:72:540:127:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:estimate the funds’ betas. When we estimate those betas using OLS, we find very similar
21:736:56369:18:18:72:540:109:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:results. To avoid using imprecise beta estimates for short-lived funds, we replace OLS betas
21:737:56461:18:18:72:540:91:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of funds having track records shorter than 24 months by the average beta of funds in the same
21:738:56554:18:0:72:540:73:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Morningstar category. Just as in Table 1, we find that the slope estimates in the bottom
22:739:56644:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:row are insignificant while the slopes in the top row are highly significant, witht-statistics
22:740:56738:18:29:72:137:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of about 7.6.
22:741:56751:29:18:89:539:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The tests described above assume that funds’ betas are time-invariant. In separate tests,
22:742:56840:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we allow funds’ betas on benchmarks or factors to vary over time in order to assess the
22:743:56927:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:extent to which turnover-related performance might reflect variation in systematic risk. If
22:744:57018:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:high turnover were associated with more systematic risk, then the higher returns following
22:745:57108:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:high turnover could represent risk compensation or simply factor timing—identifying factor-
22:746:57199:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:related mispricing. While it is not clear a priori why higher turnover should be followed
22:747:57288:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by more as opposed to less systematic risk, we nevertheless allow time variation in funds’
22:748:57378:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:betas on their Morningstar benchmarks and the factors in the four alternative factor models
22:749:57469:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:described above. In those results, the turnover-performance relation weakens only modestly,
22:750:57560:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:suggesting that relation might include some risk compensation or factor timing. In all cases,
22:751:57653:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:however, thet-statistic for the slope on turnover exceeds five. In general, turnover can reflect
22:752:57749:18:50:72:528:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:various sources of profitable trading—stock picking, industry rotation, factor timing, etc.
22:753:57840:50:41:72:315:429:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:4.  Differences Across Funds
22:754:57868:41:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our evidence so far reveals that the typical fund performs better after it trades more. Next,
22:755:57961:18:18:72:540:370:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we ask whether this time-series relation differs across funds.  We distinguish funds along
22:756:58051:18:18:72:540:352:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:four characteristics: fund size, expense ratio (or “fee,” for short), and two common style
22:757:58141:18:18:72:540:334:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:classifications—small-cap versus large-cap and value versus growth. For each of these four
22:758:58231:18:18:72:540:316:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:characteristics, we assign a fund to one of three categories. For fund size and fee, in each
22:759:58323:18:17:72:540:298:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:monthtwe compute the terciles ofF undSizei,t−1andExpenseRatioi,t−1, the most recent
22:760:58406:17:18:72:539:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:values of fundi’s assets under management and fees available from CRSP prior to montht.
22:761:58493:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For the two style classifications, we use the 3×3 “style-box” assignments of Morningstar,
22:762:58582:18:18:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which uses a fund’s holdings to classify the fund as (i) small-cap, mid-cap, or large-cap and
22:763:58675:18:18:72:540:227:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(ii) value, blend, or growth. In our sample, these two style classifications are held constant
22:764:58769:18:29:72:179:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:over a fund’s history.
22:765:58791:29:18:89:540:180:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Panels A through D of Table 2 report the estimated slope coefficients on turnover for each
22:766:58881:18:18:72:540:162:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the four characteristics used to classify funds. Each panel reports two sets of regressions.
22:767:58976:18:18:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In the first set (indicated by “Controls” as “No”), the simple regression in equation (20)
22:768:59066:18:18:72:540:126:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is run without additional control variables. The second set of regressions (with “Controls”
22:769:59157:18:18:72:540:108:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as “Yes”) controls for the other three fund characteristics by including category dummies
22:770:59246:18:18:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:interacted with lagged turnover. For the latter regressions, the slopes reported in each panel
22:771:59340:18:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:should be interpreted as applying to a fund falling in the given category of that panel’s
23:772:59431:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:characteristic and having middle-category values of the characteristics in the other three
23:773:59521:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:panels. For example, the slopes in Panel A correspond to a blend fund with medium size
23:774:59607:18:29:72:211:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and medium expense ratio.
23:775:59632:29:18:89:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Table 2 reveals a significantly positive turnover-performance relation in eight of the nine
23:776:59723:18:18:72:539:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:no-controls regressions. The only exception is large funds, having at-statistic of 1.46 (Panel
23:777:59817:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C, third column). In other words, a positive turnover-performance relation is quite pervasive
23:778:59910:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across the various subsets of funds produced by the four classifications.  The relation is
23:779:60000:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significant for small-cap funds, small funds, and high-fee funds even when we include controls,
23:780:60095:18:29:72:530:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thereby characterizing funds whose other three characteristics are in the middle category.
23:781:60185:29:18:89:540:540:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We also see in Table 2 that turnover-performance slopes are significantly larger for small-
23:782:60276:18:18:72:540:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cap funds as compared to large-cap funds (Panel A), small funds as compared to large funds
23:783:60366:18:18:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(Panel C), and high-fee funds as compared to low-fee funds (Panel D). These significant
23:784:60453:18:18:72:540:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:differences occur in both the no-controls and with-controls results, and they are rather dra-
23:785:60546:18:18:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:matic. For example, in the with-control results, small-cap funds have a slope of 0.00205
23:786:60634:18:18:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(t= 3.53), nearly seven times the large-cap slope of 0.00030 (t= 0.81). The differences
23:787:60721:18:18:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:associated with fund size and fees are similarly large. In contrast, growth and value funds
23:788:60812:18:28:72:428:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:do not exhibit a significant difference in turnover-performance slopes.
23:789:60883:28:18:89:539:386:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our model helps explain the differences across funds’ turnover-performance slopes. Con-
23:790:60970:18:18:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sider Panel A of Table 2, which shows a larger slope for small-cap funds than for large-cap
23:791:61061:18:18:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds. From equation (13), the turnover-performance slope is increasing in the trading cost
23:792:61152:18:18:72:539:332:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:per unit of turnover,c, and decreasing in the autocorrelation of turnover,ρ. If a fund has
23:793:61242:18:18:72:539:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher trading costs (higherc), then it optimally adjusts its turnover less when profit op-
23:794:61333:18:18:72:539:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:portunitiesπtchange (equation (5)). Therefore, any observed change in turnover must be
23:795:61419:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:associated with a larger change in profit opportunities and hence performance. Small-cap
23:796:61507:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stocks are generally understood to be less liquid than large-cap stocks, socis likely to be
23:797:61598:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:greater for small-cap funds. If a fund’s turnover is less persistent (lowerρ), then the profits
23:798:61693:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:from last period’s high turnover are less likely to be offset by trading costs from high turnover
23:799:61790:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this period. Table 3 shows that the turnover of small-cap funds has significantly lower au-
23:800:61881:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tocorrelation than that of large-cap funds. According to our model, having both a higher
23:801:61969:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:cand a lowerρmakes small-cap funds more likely to have a higher turnover-performance
23:802:62053:18:28:72:516:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:slope. We see from Table 2 that small-cap funds indeed have a higher estimated slope.
23:803:62138:28:18:89:540:124:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A similar interpretation applies to the results in Panel C of Table 2, which reports a
23:804:62224:18:18:72:540:106:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significantly larger turnover-performance slope for small funds than for large funds. Small
23:805:62315:18:0:72:540:88:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds, by virtue of their trading smaller dollar amounts, are better suited for trading less-
24:806:62410:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:liquid stocks than are large funds. As stock size is surely an imperfect liquidity measure,
24:807:62501:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:it seems reasonable that fund size also helps proxy for the liquidity of the fund’s holdings.
24:808:62594:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:That is, thecfor small funds is likely to be greater than for large funds, even controlling for
24:809:62689:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stock size. In addition, we see from Table 3 that small-fund turnover has a significantly lower
24:810:62784:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:autocorrelation than does large-fund turnover. Therefore, as with small-cap funds, having a
24:811:62875:18:18:72:539:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:highercand a lowerρmakes small funds more likely to have a higher turnover-performance
24:812:62961:18:28:72:281:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:slope, also consistent with our estimates.
24:813:63003:28:18:89:549:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Recall from Panel B of Table 2 that there is no significant difference in turnover-performance
24:814:63097:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:slopes for value versus growth funds.  Even this result is somewhat in keeping with our
24:815:63184:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model, in that Edelen, Evans, and Kadlec (2013) report fairly similar trading costs (per unit
24:816:63277:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of turnover) for value and growth funds, consistent withcbeing similar for both categories.
24:817:63368:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:On the other hand, we do see in Table 3 that turnover for growth funds has a significantly
24:818:63458:18:29:72:365:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher autocorrelation than does turnover of value funds.
24:819:63515:29:18:89:539:468:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The differences in turnover-performance slopes related to expense ratio, reported in Panel
24:820:63605:18:18:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:D of Table 2, must be interpreted outside our model, in which expense ratio does not appear.
24:821:63697:18:18:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Expense ratio, closely related to the management fee rate, may proxy for skill. One would
24:822:63786:18:18:72:540:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:expect managers with more skill to receive more fee revenue (e.g., Berk and Green (2004)),
24:823:63876:18:18:72:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and fee revenue is proportional to the fee rate, conditional on a given fund size. The fee
24:824:63966:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:rate is not necessarily positively correlated with skill unconditionally, as that correlation
24:825:64059:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:depends on how size covaries with fees and skill in the cross-section, but it seems reasonable
24:826:64153:17:18:72:539:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for managers with greater skill to charge higher fee rates.17Also, we find a higher slope
24:827:64242:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for high-fee funds regardless of whether we condition on fund size by including controls
24:828:64330:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in Panel D. Less-skilled (and thus lower-fee) funds are likely to have a lower turnover-
24:829:64418:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance slope, because they tend to make two mistakes. First, they sometimes trade
24:830:64504:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:too much, perceiving profit opportunities that do not really exist. Consistent with this idea,
24:831:64598:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Christoffersen and Sarkissian (2011) argue that overconfidence sometimes leads mutual funds
24:832:64689:18:18:72:539:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:to trade too much.18Second, less-skilled funds sometimes trade too little, failing to perceive
24:833:64783:18:18:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:profit opportunities that truly exist. Because of these mistakes, some of the time variation
24:834:64875:18:18:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in a less-skilled fund’s turnover is unrelated to time variation in true profit opportunities,
24:835:64969:18:18:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:producing a weaker turnover-performance relation. If a fund is so unskilled that its turnover
24:836:65062:18:15:81:540:163:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:17Consistent with this idea, Kacperczyk, van Nieuwerburgh, and Veldkamp (2014) report that funds with
24:837:65163:15:9:72:373:148:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:superior stock-picking skill charge significantly higher expense ratios.
24:838:65235:9:15:81:540:139:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:18Christoffersen and Sarkissian (2011) find that excessive trading is more prevalent among fund managers
24:839:65339:15:12:72:540:124:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:working in major financial centers. They also find that excess turnover declines with experience, consistent
24:840:65447:12:12:72:540:112:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:with overconfident managers gradually learning their true ability. While the authors’ focus is on demographic
24:841:65556:12:12:72:540:100:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:determinants of turnover, they also report a mixed relation between turnover and performance based on panel
24:842:65663:12:0:72:320:88:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:regressions similar to ours but without fund fixed effects.
25:843:65724:0:29:72:343:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is pure noise, the turnover-performance slope is zero.
25:844:65778:29:18:89:540:694:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Besides fees, we consider two additional proxies for fund skill. First, we take a fund’s
25:845:65866:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gross alpha over the fund’s lifetime. Second, we compute gross alpha adjusted for both fund-
25:846:65958:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:level and industry-level returns to scale, following P ́astor, Stambaugh, and Taylor (2015).
25:847:66050:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:For both proxies, we find that high-skill funds exhibit a significantly stronger turnover-
25:848:66140:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance relation than low-skill funds. These results, which are consistent with those in
25:849:66232:17:29:72:326:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Table 2 based on fees, are in the online appendix.
25:850:66282:29:18:89:540:576:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The appendix also shows the results from an exercise that takes a different perspective
25:851:66369:18:18:72:540:558:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:on skill. Del Guercio and Reuter (2014) argue that broker-sold mutual funds face a weaker
25:852:66458:18:18:72:540:540:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:incentive to generate alpha than funds sold directly to retail investors. Motivated by their
25:853:66550:18:18:72:540:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:evidence, we compare the strength of the turnover-performance relation across these market
25:854:66640:18:18:72:539:504:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:segments.19We find that the relation is somewhat stronger in direct-sold funds than in
25:855:66726:18:18:72:540:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:broker-sold funds. The turnover-performance slope is 40% larger in magnitude for direct-
25:856:66814:18:18:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sold funds, but the slope difference is not statistically significant (thep-value is 15%). While
25:857:66910:18:18:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:this evidence is inconclusive, it points in the direction of direct-sold funds having a stronger
25:858:67006:18:29:72:426:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:incentive to perform, consistent with Del Guercio and Reuter (2014).
25:859:67074:29:17:89:539:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Finally, the average gross fund returns reported in Table 3 are also consistent with the
25:860:67162:17:18:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model, in two ways.  In each of the four panels of Table 3, the average gross return of
25:861:67249:18:18:72:540:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the top category is significantly greater than the bottom category.  The same is true for
25:862:67338:18:18:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:two other quantities that our model predicts to be related to expected gross return: average
25:863:67430:18:18:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover (Table 3) and the turnover-performance slope (Table 2). The observed link between
25:864:67520:18:18:72:540:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the average gross return and average turnover is consistent with the model’s prediction of
25:865:67610:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:a positive cross-sectional turnover-performance relation (cf. equations (14) and (15)), and
25:866:67701:18:18:72:539:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:also with the positive cross-sectional slope estimate in Table 1.20The observed link to the
25:867:67792:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover-performance slope is consistent with equations (13) through (15).  According to
25:868:67880:18:18:72:539:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:equation (13), the slope should be larger for funds with higher values ofcandθ, holdingρ
25:869:67968:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:constant. According to equations (14) and (15), funds with highercandθshould also have
25:870:68054:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher expected gross returns, holding average turnover constant. Interestingly, the only top-
25:871:68148:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:minus-bottom difference for which the slope in Table 2 is insignificant, growth minus value,
25:872:68240:18:17:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is also the only difference for which the average gross return in Table 3 is only marginally
25:873:68332:17:16:81:540:153:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:19To classify fund share classes by distribution channel, we use the approximation method of Sun (2014).
25:874:68436:16:12:72:540:137:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:We treat a share class as broker-sold if it has a non-zero front load, non-zero back load, or 12b-1 fee exceeding
25:875:68549:12:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:25 bps; otherwise, we treat it as direct-sold. Following Del Guercio and Reuter (2014), we classify a fund as
25:876:68658:12:8:72:518:113:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:broker-sold (direct-sold) if at least 75% of its assets are broker-sold (direct-sold) on average over time.
25:877:68765:8:16:81:540:105:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:20This evidence is also consistent with the result of Kacperczyk, van Nieuwerburgh, and Veldkamp (2014)
25:878:68868:16:0:72:447:89:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:that funds with superior stock-picking skill have significantly higher average turnover.
26:879:68958:0:51:72:297:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significant, which jibes well with the model.
26:880:69003:51:40:72:478:672:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:5.  The Common Component of Fund Turnover
26:881:69044:40:18:72:540:632:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Given our focus on the time variation in fund turnover, it seems natural to examine the
26:882:69131:18:18:72:540:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:extent to which this variation is common across funds. In this section, we aggregate turnover
26:883:69224:18:18:72:540:596:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across funds and explore its time variation. In Section 5.1, we analyze comovement in fund
26:884:69314:18:18:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover.  In Section 5.2, we investigate the determinants of the common component of
26:885:69399:18:18:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover. Finally, in Section 5.3, we study the predictive power of the common component
26:886:69487:18:45:72:183:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for fund performance.
26:887:69508:45:37:72:292:497:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5.1.  Commonality in Turnover
26:888:69537:37:18:72:539:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In our model, time variation in fund turnover is driven by variation in the fund’s profit
26:889:69626:18:18:72:540:442:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:opportunities. Those opportunities are likely to be positively correlated across funds. Any
26:890:69717:18:18:72:540:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mispriced stock presents a profit opportunity to many different funds that can potentially
26:891:69807:18:18:72:540:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:trade this stock. Moreover, if mispricing has market-wide causes such as liquidity disruptions
26:892:69901:18:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:or investor sentiment, many stocks can be mispriced at the same time. If profit opportunities
26:893:69994:18:28:72:506:370:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are indeed correlated across funds, the model predicts comovement in fund turnover.
26:894:70077:28:18:89:539:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To see whether such comovement exists, we first compute category-level averages of
26:895:70159:18:18:72:540:324:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:individual fund turnover. We consider the same fund categories as before: three stock-size
26:896:70249:18:18:72:540:306:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:categories, three value-growth categories, three fund-size categories, and three expense-ratio
26:897:70343:18:18:72:540:288:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:categories.  For each category, we compute the average turnover across all funds in that
26:898:70431:18:18:72:540:270:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:category. Specifically, average turnover in monthtis the equal-weighted average turnover
26:899:70519:18:29:72:451:252:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across category funds in the 12-month fiscal period that includes montht.
26:900:70592:29:18:89:539:223:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Figure 1 plots the time series of the category-level average turnover over the 1979-2011
26:901:70680:18:18:72:540:205:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:period.  The figure shows strong comovement in turnover.  The times series of average
26:902:70765:18:18:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover are highly correlated both within and across the four panels.  For example, the
26:903:70853:18:18:72:540:169:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:correlation between the average turnovers of small-cap and large-cap funds, both of which
26:904:70942:18:18:72:540:151:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are plotted in Panel A, is 59%. We observe similar correlations, ranging from 52% to 61%,
26:905:71031:18:17:72:540:133:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between the average turnovers of value and growth funds (Panel B), small and large funds
26:906:71119:17:18:72:540:116:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(Panel C), and high-fee and low-fee funds (Panel D). All pairwise correlations within each
26:907:71209:18:18:72:540:98:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:panel are reported in Table 4. In the context of our model, this evidence of comovement
26:908:71296:18:0:72:540:80:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in turnover indicates that profit opportunities are positively correlated across funds—even
27:909:71389:0:29:72:287:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across funds with different characteristics.
27:910:71433:29:18:89:540:694:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Panel B of Figure 1 provides more evidence on the result from Table 3 that growth funds
27:911:71520:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turn over more than value funds. Interestingly, the turnover of growth funds exceeds that of
27:912:71612:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:value funds not only on average but also in every single year, and by a wide margin. Value
27:913:71702:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds appear to be more patient than growth funds in exploiting their profit opportunities.
27:914:71793:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We also see in Panel D that more expensive funds tend to turn over more than cheaper
27:915:71877:17:29:72:424:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:funds. The patterns in Panels A and C are less consistent over time.
27:916:71945:29:18:89:539:576:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In addition to computing average turnover at the category level, we compute it at the
27:917:72030:18:18:72:540:558:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:aggregate level. We letAvgT urndenote the average of individual fund turnover computed
27:918:72116:18:18:72:540:540:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across all funds. Analogous to the category-level variable,AvgT urntis the average turnover
27:919:72207:18:18:72:540:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across funds’ 12-month fiscal periods that contain montht.AvgT urnt, plotted in Panel A
27:920:72294:18:18:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of Figure 2, fluctuates between 59% and 102% per year from 1979 to 2011.21It has a 95%
27:921:72380:18:18:72:540:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:correlation with the first principal component of individual fund turnover. Therefore, we
27:922:72469:18:29:72:481:468:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:viewAvgT urntas the simplest measure of the common component of turnover.
27:923:72542:29:18:89:540:439:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:To shed more light on commonality in turnover, we regress individual fund turnover in
27:924:72627:18:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:monthton its common component,AvgT urnt.22To isolate time-series variation in turnover,
27:925:72714:18:17:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:we run a panel regression with fund fixed effects. We report the results in the first column
27:926:72806:17:18:72:539:386:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of Table 5.  The slope coefficient from the regression ofF undT urnonAvgT urnis 0.65
27:927:72890:18:29:72:409:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(t= 8.65), indicating strong evidence of commonality in turnover.
27:928:72955:29:18:89:539:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The evidence of commonality strengthens further when we add category-level average
27:929:73037:18:18:72:540:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover to the right-hand side of the above regression.  For each fundi, we calculate
27:930:73123:18:18:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:AvgT urnStockSizeas the average turnover across funds in the same stock-size category
27:931:73208:18:18:72:539:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:as fundi. In the regression ofF undT urnon bothAvgT urnandAvgT urnStockSize, the
27:932:73288:18:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:category-level average is highly significant (t= 5.27), the sum of the slopes on the two aver-
27:933:73382:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ages is again 0.65, and theR2increases by almost half. We also calculate average turnover
27:934:73471:18:18:72:539:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across funds in the same value-growth category (AvgT urnStockV G), same fund-size cate-
27:935:73558:18:17:72:542:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:gory (AvgT urnF undSize), and same expense-ratio category (AvgT urnF undExp). While
27:936:73641:17:18:72:540:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the value-growth average is insignificant when added to the above regression, the other
27:937:73728:18:18:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:two averages produce results very similar to those obtained for the stock-size average: the
27:938:73819:18:16:81:540:160:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:21CRSP turnover data are missing in 1991 for unknown reasons. We therefore treatAvgT urnas missing
27:939:73917:16:12:72:540:144:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:in 1991 in our regressions. In Figure 2, though, we fill in average turnover in 1991 by using Morningstar data,
27:940:74028:12:12:72:540:132:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:for aesthetic purposes. We rely on CRSP turnover data in our analysis because Morningstar is ambiguous
27:941:74130:12:8:72:240:120:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:about the timing of funds’ fiscal years.
27:942:74170:8:16:81:539:112:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:22For the purpose of this regression, we recalculateAvgT urntcorresponding to each fundias the average
27:943:74272:16:12:72:540:96:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:turnover across all fundsj6=i. By excluding fundifrom the calculation of average turnover, we exclude
27:944:74373:12:12:72:540:84:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:any mechanical correlation that could create a spurious perception of commonality. Analogously, we exclude
27:945:74479:12:0:72:456:72:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:fundifrom all other measures of average turnover discussed in the following paragraph.
28:946:74567:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:category-level average is highly significant, the sum of the slopes on the two averages is a bit
28:947:74663:18:18:72:539:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:larger than 0.65, and theR2increases by almost half. Finally, we calculate average turnover
28:948:74754:18:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:across “similar” funds,AvgT urnSim, by averaging across funds in the same stock-size,
28:949:74839:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund-size, and expense-ratio categories. (We exclude value-growth due to its insignificance
28:950:74930:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:observed earlier.) When added to the above regression, this variable comes in highly sig-
28:951:75019:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:nificant (t= 7.35), the sum of the slopes onAvgT urnandAvgT urnSimis 0.68, and the
28:952:75101:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:R2almost doubles. This evidence, which is reported in Table 5, shows that commonality in
28:953:75189:18:45:72:430:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover is especially strong among funds with similar characteristics.
28:954:75260:45:36:72:275:552:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5.2.  Mispricing and Trading
28:955:75288:36:18:72:540:516:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:When do funds trade more than usual? In our model, funds trade more when their profit
28:956:75373:18:18:72:540:498:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:opportunities are better. If such opportunities arise from mispricing, then funds should trade
28:957:75467:18:18:72:540:480:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more in periods with more mispricing. We thus ask whether fund turnover is higher when
28:958:75553:18:18:72:539:462:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mispricing is more likely. We use three proxies for the likelihood of mispricing:Sentimentt,
28:959:75645:18:29:72:460:444:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:V olatilityt, andLiquidityt. We plot the three series in Panel B of Figure 2.
28:960:75722:29:18:89:540:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The first mispricing proxy,Sentimentt, is the value in monthtof Baker and Wurgler’s
28:961:75805:18:18:72:540:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(2006, 2007) investor-sentiment index. If sentiment-driven investors participate more heav-
28:962:75896:18:18:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ily in the stock market during high-sentiment periods, the mispricing such investors create
28:963:75987:18:18:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is more likely to occur during those periods (e.g., Stambaugh, Yu, and Yuan, 2012). We
28:964:76073:18:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thus expect funds exploiting such mispricing to trade more when sentiment is high. Con-
28:965:76160:18:18:72:539:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:sistent with this prediction, time-series regressions of bothF undT urni,tandAvgT urnton
28:966:76248:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Sentimenttproduce significantly positive slope coefficients (t= 3.35 andt= 3.17, respec-
28:967:76336:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tively), as shown in columns 1 and 5 of Table 6. We include a time trend in both regressions,
28:968:76429:18:17:72:539:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:given the positive trend inAvgT urntevident in Figure 2. The time trend is significant in
28:969:76518:17:18:72:539:254:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:the latter regression but not in the former. As reported in the last row of of Table 6, theR2
28:970:76611:18:18:72:539:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in the regression ofAvgT urntonSentimenttand the time trend exceeds theR2from the
28:971:76692:18:18:72:540:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:regression on the time trend alone by 0.171. Sentiment, in other words, explains a substantial
28:972:76786:18:29:72:365:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fraction of the time variation in aggregate fund turnover.
28:973:76844:29:18:89:540:171:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The second mispricing proxy,V olatilityt, is the cross-sectional standard deviation in
28:974:76930:18:18:72:539:153:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:monthtof the returns on individual U.S. stocks.23The rationale for this variable is that
28:975:77018:18:18:72:540:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher volatility corresponds to greater uncertainty about future values and thus greater
28:976:77107:18:18:72:540:117:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:potential for investors to err in assessing those values. As a result, periods of high volatility
28:977:77204:18:18:72:540:99:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:admit greater potential mispricing, and we expect funds exploiting such mispricing to trade
28:978:77295:18:0:81:297:81:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:23We thank Bryan Kelly for providing this series.
29:979:77346:0:18:72:539:723:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f9:more when volatility is high. Consistent with this prediction, regressions of bothF undT urni,t
29:980:77441:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:andAvgT urntonV olatilitytproduce significantly positive slopes (t= 7.78 andt= 7.23,
29:981:77525:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:respectively), as shown in columns 2 and 6 of Table 6. TheR2in the latter regression, which
29:982:77616:18:29:72:489:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:again includes a time trend, exceeds theR2in the trend-only regression by 0.188.
29:983:77696:29:18:89:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The third proxy,Liquidityt, is the value in monthtof the stock-market liquidity measure
29:984:77783:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of P ́astor and Stambaugh (2003). Empirical evidence suggests that higher liquidity is accom-
29:985:77876:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:panied by greater market efficiency (e.g., Chordia, Roll, and Subrahmanyam, 2008, 2011).
29:986:77964:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:In other words, periods of lower liquidity are more susceptible to mispricing. Therefore, we
29:987:78056:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:might expect funds to trade more when liquidity is lower. On the other hand, lower liquid-
29:988:78146:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ity also implies higher transaction costs, which could discourage funds from trading. Our
29:989:78235:18:18:72:539:533:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f9:evidence suggests that the former effect is stronger: RegressingF undT urni,tandAvgT urnt
29:990:78324:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:onLiquiditytyields significantly negative slope estimates (t=−4.55 andt=−4.14, respec-
29:991:78410:18:18:72:539:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tively), reported in columns 3 and 7 of Table 6. IncludingLiquiditytincreases theR2versus
29:992:78499:18:29:72:481:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the trend-only regression by a more modest amount than the other two proxies.
29:993:78576:29:18:89:540:450:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:When all three mispricing proxies are included simultaneously as regressors, each enters
29:994:78664:18:18:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:with a coefficient andt-statistic very similar to when included just by itself.  These all-
29:995:78755:18:18:72:540:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:inclusive regressions, reported in columns 4 and 8 of Table 6, also add two additional variables
29:996:78851:18:18:72:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:that control for potential effects of the business cycle and recent stock-market returns, but
29:997:78944:18:18:72:541:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:neither variable enters significantly. (The two variables are the Chicago Fed National Activity
29:998:79039:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Index and the return on the CRSP value-weighted market index over the previous 12 months.)
29:999:79129:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The combined ability of the three mispricing proxies to explain variance inAvgT urntis
29:1000:79215:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:substantial: theR2exceeds that of the trend-only regression by 0.324.24Overall, the results
29:1001:79306:18:29:72:386:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:make sense: funds trade more when there is more mispricing.
29:1002:79365:29:18:89:540:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:What mispricing are funds exploiting? To see whether funds trade based on well-known
29:1003:79449:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:market anomalies, we regress the returns of eleven such anomalies, as well as their composite
29:1004:79542:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:return, on lagged average fund turnover. The eleven anomalies, whose returns we obtain from
29:1005:79633:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Stambaugh, Yu, and Yuan (2012), involve sorting stocks based on two measures of financial
29:1006:79722:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:distress, two measures of stock issuance, accruals, net operating assets, momentum, gross
29:1007:79811:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:profitability, asset growth, return on assets, and the investment-to-assets ratio. We find no
29:1008:79904:18:17:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:significant slopes on average turnover. To the extent that funds trade more when there is
29:1009:79993:17:16:81:540:153:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:24If we exclude the time trend from the regressions, we find results similar to those reported in Table 6.
29:1010:80099:16:12:72:540:137:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f7:V olatilityandLiquiditycontinue to enter significantly with the same signs as in Table 6, and the business
29:1011:80205:12:12:72:539:125:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:cycle and market return remain insignificant. The only difference relates toSentiment, whose coefficient
29:1012:80309:12:12:72:539:113:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:retains the positive sign but loses statistical significance in the regression that involvesAvgT urn(it remains
29:1013:80420:12:12:72:539:101:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:significant in the regression that involvesF undT urn). This evidence suggests thatSentimentis better at
29:1014:80524:12:0:72:498:89:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:capturing deviations ofAvgT urnfrom its trend than in capturing the raw variation inAvgT urn.
30:1015:80619:0:29:72:477:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more mispricing, they are exploiting mispricing beyond these eleven anomalies.
30:1016:80697:29:18:89:540:694:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Finally, we consider the role of stock market turnover in explainingAvgT urnt.  We
30:1017:80779:18:18:72:540:676:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measure market turnover as total dollar volume over the previous 12 months divided by
30:1018:80864:18:18:72:540:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:total market capitalization of ordinary common shares in CRSP. Market turnover reflects
30:1019:80951:18:18:72:539:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:trading by all entities, including mutual funds, so it could potentially be related toAvgT urnt.
30:1020:81047:18:17:72:539:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:It could also be related toSentimentt, which is constructed as the first principal component
30:1021:81139:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of six variables that include NYSE turnover. However, when we add market turnover to
30:1022:81223:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the all-inclusive specification in column 8 of Table 6, it does not enter significantly, whereas
30:1023:81319:18:18:72:539:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the slope onSentimenttremains positive and significant. The other two mispricing proxies
30:1024:81407:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:also retain their signs and significance, and the remaining variables remain insignificant. In
30:1025:81501:18:45:72:439:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:short, adding market turnover does not affect our inferences in Table 6.
30:1026:81573:45:37:72:318:488:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5.3.  Predicting Fund Performance
30:1027:81606:37:18:72:539:451:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Given its significant link to the mispricing proxies, it is natural to ask whether the common
30:1028:81699:18:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:component of fund turnover helps predict fund performance.  In fact, a positive relation
30:1029:81787:18:18:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:between the common component and future performance can be motivated directly within
30:1030:81871:18:18:72:539:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our model. In the model, optimal fund turnover,X∗tfrom equation (5), results solely from
30:1031:81959:18:18:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:the fund’s decision to change the composition of its portfolio. In the data, however, inflows
30:1032:82052:18:17:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and outflows of investors’ capital also give rise to trading by the fund. The reported turnover
30:1033:82147:17:18:72:540:344:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measure that we observe empirically, ̃Xt, abstracts from flow effects, but only imperfectly,
30:1034:82239:18:18:72:540:326:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:so it is not precisely equal toX∗t. There could also be other reasons why a fund’s observed
30:1035:82330:18:25:72:514:308:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover could differ from its true, optimally chosen value. In other words, we observe
30:1036:82417:25:30:271:540:283:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: ̃Xt=X∗t+ut,(23)
30:1037:82433:30:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:whereutdenotes the measurement error.  We assume thatuthas mean zero and is un-
30:1038:82512:18:18:72:539:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:correlated withX∗t. With many funds in the market, an additional explanatory variable
30:1039:82597:18:18:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:useful in addressing this error-in-variable problem is the cross-sectional average turnover,
30:1040:82689:18:18:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:which we denote byXt. Intuitively, since turnover comoves across funds, average turnover
30:1041:82777:18:18:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:contains additional information about a fund’s true turnover beyond the information in our
30:1042:82867:18:18:72:539:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:imperfectF undT urnmeasure. We assume that there are sufficiently many funds that the
30:1043:82952:18:27:72:441:145:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:measurement errors in turnover diversify away when computingXt. Let
30:1044:83019:27:28:259:540:118:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:X∗t=βXXt+φt,(24)
30:1045:83035:28:18:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and assume thatφtis uncorrelated withXtand that the residualsφt,ut, and-t+1are mutually
30:1046:83122:18:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:uncorrelated. Letσ2uandσ2φdenote the variances ofutandφt, respectively. Consider the
31:1047:83208:0:26:72:526:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:linear regression of the fund’s returnRt+1on fund turnover ̃Xtand average turnoverXt:
31:1048:83293:26:26:222:540:697:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:Rt+1=ˆθ0+ˆθ1 ̃Xt+ˆθ2Xt+et+1.(25)
31:1049:83325:26:30:72:451:671:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:As we show in the Appendix, the slope coefficients have probability limits
31:1050:83399:30:0:250:279:641:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:θ1=

31:1062:83443:31:18:72:540:575:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Bothθ1andθ2are positive as long asbfrom equation (11) andβXfrom equation (24) are
31:1063:83524:18:17:72:540:557:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:positive, which is consistent with the data (see Tables 1 and 5). Moreover, the coefficient on
31:1064:83618:17:18:72:539:540:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:average turnover (θ2) is large when the measurement error in turnover is large (i.e.,σ2ularge)
31:1065:83712:18:18:72:539:522:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and when the commonality in turnover is large (i.e.,σ2φsmall). Given our strong evidence of
31:1066:83803:18:29:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:commonality, our model suggests a role for average turnover in predicting fund performance.
31:1067:83894:29:18:89:540:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We find such a role in the data.  We run a panel regression of the gross benchmark-
31:1068:83977:18:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:adjusted fund return (GrossRi,t) on average lagged turnover, with fund fixed effects. We de-
31:1069:84069:18:18:72:540:439:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:note average lagged turnover, or the average ofF undT urnj,t−1acrossj6=i, byAvgT urnt−1.25

31:1071:84244:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The slope is positive and significant (t= 2.25), indicating that the common component of
31:1072:84332:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund trading helps predict individual fund performance. The magnitude of the estimate,
31:1073:84418:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:0.00784, implies substantial economic significance. Given the time-series standard deviation
31:1074:84510:18:18:72:539:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ofAvgT urnt−1, 0.076, a one-standard-deviation increase in the variable translates to an
31:1075:84598:18:28:72:450:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:increase in expected return of 0.71% per year (= 0.00784×0.076×1200).
31:1076:84667:28:18:89:540:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The information inAvgT urnt−1about a fund’s subsequent performance is undiminished
31:1077:84749:18:18:72:540:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:by conditioning on the fund’s own turnover. Column 4 of Table 7 shows that the coeffi-
31:1078:84835:18:18:72:539:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cient andt-statistic forAvgT urnt−1are little changed by controlling forF undT urni,t−1.
31:1079:84923:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Similarly, the significance of the slope onF undT urni,t−1is little changed by controlling for
31:1080:85017:18:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:AvgT urnt−1. The fund’s performance is predictable by both average turnover and the fund’s
31:1081:85107:18:17:72:516:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:own turnover. In the context of our model, we findˆθ1>0 andˆθ2>0 in equation (25).
31:1082:85189:17:16:81:540:196:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:25We omit theisubscript fromAvgT urni,t−1because excluding fundifrom the average makes very little
31:1083:85287:16:12:72:540:180:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:difference. Note thatAvgT urnt−1uses only information available before monthtbecause it is the average of
31:1084:85392:12:12:72:539:168:10:g_d0_f7:7:g_d0_f6:turnovers computed over 12-month periods that end before montht. It is thus reasonable to useAvgT urnt−1
31:1085:85496:12:12:72:539:156:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:to predict performance in montht. Also note that the notation for time subscripts is complicated by the fact
31:1086:85604:12:12:72:539:144:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:that funds report turnover only annually. In Section 5.1, we use the notationAvgT urntto denote average
31:1087:85707:12:12:72:539:132:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:turnover across funds’ 12-month fiscal periods that contain montht. That notation is slightly inconsistent
31:1088:85813:12:12:72:540:120:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:with the notation in this section because given our definition ofF undT urni,t, the contemporaneous average
31:1089:85920:12:12:72:539:108:10:g_d0_f7:7:g_d0_f18:turnover in Section 5.1 is the average ofF undT urni,t+11acrossi. We prefer to use the notationAvgT urnt
31:1090:86024:12:12:72:540:96:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:(instead ofAvgT urnt+11) in Section 5.1 to emphasize the contemporaneous nature of the analysis in that
31:1091:86127:12:8:72:376:84:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:section. We hope the reader will pardon this slight abuse of notation.
31:1092:86197:8:0:81:518:76:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:26The regressions in Table 7 exclude a time trend, but the results are very similar if we include one.
32:1093:86301:0:18:89:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The above discussion suggests the predictive power of average turnover is due to common-
32:1094:86389:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ality in turnover. Since this commonality is stronger among funds with similar characteristics
32:1095:86483:18:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:(recall Table 5), the predictive power of average turnover might improve if the average is
32:1096:86573:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:computed across only similar funds. To examine this hypothesis, we regressGrossRi,ton
32:1097:86658:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:AvgT urnSimt−1.27Column 2 of Table 7 shows that the slope onAvgT urnSimt−1is posi-
32:1098:86740:18:18:72:539:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tive and significant (t= 3.69), and column 5 shows that it remains so when controlling for
32:1099:86830:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f4:F undT urni,t−1. In column 6, we consider the regression in which both average turnovers are
32:1100:86922:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:included, along withF undT urni,t−1. In this horserace,AvgT urnSimt−1remains positive
32:1101:87007:18:18:72:539:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and significant whereasAvgT urnt−1turns insignificant. The variable that better captures
32:1102:87095:18:28:72:487:561:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:commonality in turnover is thus more important in predicting fund performance.
32:1103:87173:28:18:89:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We have shown that a fund’s performance is predictable not only by the fund’s own
32:1104:87254:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover but also by the average turnover of other funds, especially similar funds. We have
32:1105:87345:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:motivated this result in the context of our model, based on the commonality in turnover
32:1106:87432:18:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and measurement error. The turnover of other funds can also predict performance for other
32:1107:87521:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:reasons that are outside the model. For example, in the model, funds always trade optimally,
32:1108:87613:18:29:72:539:443:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:but suboptimal trading can also create a predictive role forAvgT urnt−1, as we explain next.
32:1109:87705:29:18:89:540:414:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Suppose that funds trade suboptimally, so that only a fraction of a typical fund’s turnover
32:1110:87796:18:18:72:540:396:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:involves exploiting true profit opportunities. Also suppose that funds’ profit opportunities
32:1111:87888:18:18:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are positively correlated. This setting can arise, for example, if some stocks are mispriced
32:1112:87980:18:17:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:while others are not, funds trade both types of stocks (the latter erroneously), and the
32:1113:88068:17:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:degree of mispricing in the former stocks varies over time in a way that many funds can
32:1114:88155:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:exploit.  In this setting, as long as funds’ deviations from optimal trading are approxi-
32:1115:88244:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:mately uncorrelated, heavier trading by other funds indicates more mispricing. Therefore,
32:1116:88333:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:not onlyF undT urni,t−1but alsoAvgT urnt−1can predict performance.F undT urni,t−1is
32:1117:88416:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher—and fundi’s subsequent performance is better—when fundi’s own manager identifies
32:1118:88503:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more profit opportunities. When many managers identify such opportunities,AvgT urnt−1is
32:1119:88590:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:higher, and there is more mispricing in general. Even when a fund’s own manager does not
32:1120:88678:18:18:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:identify unusually many opportunities in a given period, the opportunities he does identify
32:1121:88769:18:29:72:497:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:are likely to be more profitable if there is generally more mispricing in that period.
32:1122:88855:29:18:89:540:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:The same story can also explain whyAvgT urnSimt−1drives outAvgT urnt−1in column
32:1123:88934:18:17:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:6 of Table 7.  If trading by other funds signals the presence of greater mispricing, then
32:1124:89023:17:18:72:540:135:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:heavier trading by funds similar to one’s own could signal greater mispricing that is especially
32:1125:89119:18:18:72:540:117:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relevant. In other words, heavier trading by less-similar funds could be less relevant to one’s
32:1126:89214:18:18:72:540:99:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:own fund. This possibility is consistent with our evidence that the turnover of one’s own
32:1127:89303:18:0:81:475:81:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:27As we did forAvgT urnt−1, we exclude fundifrom the average yet omit theisubscript.
33:1128:89389:0:51:72:399:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:fund typically comoves more with the turnover of similar funds.
33:1129:89452:51:40:72:203:672:17:g_d0_f3:17:g_d0_f3:6.  Conclusions
33:1130:89467:40:18:72:540:632:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We develop a model of fund trading in the presence of time-varying profit opportunities. The
33:1131:89559:18:18:72:540:614:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:model’s key implication is a positive time-series relation between an active fund’s turnover
33:1132:89651:18:18:72:541:596:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and its subsequent benchmark-adjusted return. We find strong support for this implication
33:1133:89740:18:18:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in a comprehensive sample of equity mutual funds. Funds exhibit an ability to identify time-
33:1134:89832:18:18:72:541:560:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:varying profit opportunities and adjust their trading activity accordingly. This time-series
33:1135:89924:18:18:72:540:542:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:relation between turnover and performance is stronger than the cross-sectional relation, as
33:1136:90015:18:18:72:540:524:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:our model predicts. The model also predicts a stronger time-series relation for funds trading
33:1137:90108:18:17:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:less-liquid stocks. Indeed, we find a stronger relation for small-stock funds and small funds.
33:1138:90202:17:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We also find a stronger relation for funds with higher fees, consistent with such funds having
33:1139:90296:18:29:72:379:471:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:greater skill in identifying time-varying profit opportunities.
33:1140:90359:29:18:89:540:442:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:We provide strong evidence of commonality in mutual fund turnover. Turnover’s common
33:1141:90443:18:18:72:540:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:component, average turnover, is positively correlated with mispricing proxies. Funds trade
33:1142:90533:18:18:72:540:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:more when investor sentiment is high, when cross-sectional stock volatility is high, and when
33:1143:90626:18:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:stock market liquidity is low, consistent with funds identifying more profit opportunities
33:1144:90716:18:18:72:540:370:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:in periods when mispricing is more likely. The common component of turnover positively
33:1145:90802:18:18:72:540:352:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:predicts fund returns, even controlling for the fund’s own turnover. This predictive ability of
33:1146:90897:18:18:72:540:334:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:average turnover is consistent with an individual fund’s observed turnover being a noisy proxy
33:1147:90991:18:18:72:540:316:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:for the fund’s true turnover. Turnover’s common component helps capture a fund’s true
33:1148:91076:18:17:72:540:298:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover and thereby helps predict the fund’s performance. Average turnover’s predictive
33:1149:91164:17:18:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ability is also consistent with suboptimal trading by funds, where only some trades exploit
33:1150:91255:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:true profit opportunities.  Whatever true opportunities a fund does identify are likely to
33:1151:91345:18:18:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:be more profitable when turnover’s common component is high. Commonality in turnover
33:1152:91429:18:18:72:540:227:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:is especially high among funds sharing similar characteristics, and a fund’s performance is
33:1153:91520:18:29:72:433:209:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:predicted even more strongly by the average turnover of similar funds.
33:1154:91590:29:18:89:540:180:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Heavier trading by funds when mispricing is more likely underscores the role of active
33:1155:91676:18:18:72:540:162:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:management in the price discovery process. While the active management industry may not
33:1156:91763:18:18:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:provide superior net returns to its investors (consistent with both theory and evidence), it
33:1157:91855:18:18:72:540:126:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:creates a valuable externality. The combined trading of many funds helps correct prices and
33:1158:91946:18:18:72:540:108:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:thereby enables more efficient capital allocation. French (2008) characterizes his estimated
33:1159:92038:18:18:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:cost of active management as a societal cost of price discovery. Stambaugh’s (2014) calibra-
33:1160:92130:18:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:tion of a general equilibrium model implies that active management corrects a large portion
34:1161:92223:0:18:72:540:723:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of the mispricing that would otherwise exist in the presence of noise traders. Our results
34:1162:92313:18:18:72:540:705:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:support this view of active management’s societal value, given our evidence that funds have
34:1163:92404:18:29:72:483:687:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:skill and that they more actively apply that skill when mispricing is more likely.
34:1164:92486:29:18:89:539:658:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Our study could be extended in several directions. For example, while we relate funds’
34:1165:92572:18:18:72:540:640:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:turnover to their future performance, it could also be interesting to relate turnover to fund
34:1166:92665:18:17:72:540:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:flows. Such analysis would reveal whether fund investors are aware of turnover’s ability to
34:1167:92756:17:18:72:540:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:predict returns. In the Berk and Green (2004) model, investors respond to fund returns,
34:1168:92843:18:18:72:540:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:but our results suggest that they might also benefit from responding to turnover. Another
34:1169:92932:18:18:72:540:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:promising direction is to go beyond turnover and analyze the funds’ trading activity in more
34:1170:93024:18:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:detail. For example, one could analyze changes in fund holdings or adjust turnover for non-
34:1171:93115:18:18:72:540:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:discretionary trading. Such analysis could potentially produce even more powerful predictors
34:1172:93207:18:18:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:of future fund performance.  Finally, finding exogenous variation in profit opportunities
34:1173:93296:18:18:72:540:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:and funds’ ability to exploit them would help identify any causal relations between fund
34:1174:93384:18:0:72:485:479:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:performance, trading, and mispricing. We leave these challenges for future work.

39:1654:99291:14:15:72:540:151:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:ratio, splitting the sample each month into terciles based on their lagged expense ratio. We
